By nature, an interlude contrasts with the activity it interrupts or the events it comes between ?often occurring as an interval of calm, a time of content or a touch of comic relief: interludes of lucidity in his delirium; a humorous interlude in a sober history; Their honeymoon was an idyllic interlude. Intermission and interval are synonyms for a scheduled recess between the acts of a play or the parts of a performance: to go out for a smoke during intermission. Interlude, on the other hand, may apply to an entertainment of a different kind that fills a break between the acts, as a brief, farcical comedy or a short, transitional passage of music: an orchestral interlude. In another sense, intermission may apply to any temporary cessation: The noise went on without intermission.

间奏是在一个较长的过程中发生的一段或一段插曲，它打破了它的连续性：从本质上讲，间奏与它中断的活动或它之间发生的事件形成鲜明对比——通常作为一个间隔发生。平静的时光，一段满足的时光或一丝喜剧般的轻松：他的谵妄中的清醒的插曲；清醒的历史中的幽默插曲；他们的蜜月是一段田园诗般的插曲，是一场演出之间预定的休息的同义词。戏剧或表演的一部分：在幕间休息时出去抽烟，另一方面，插曲可能适用于填补表演之间休息的不同类型的娱乐，如简短的滑稽喜剧或短片。 ，音乐的过渡段落：管弦乐间奏 在另一种意义上，间歇可以适用于任何暂时的停止：噪音不间断地继续。

Let-up is an informal word and is usually used negatively after no or without. It often indicates abatement rather than cessation, pointing to a lessening of force, a slackening of pace or a reduction in number or intensity. [The rain poured down without let-up; We’ve worked two hours without let-up; There has been no let-up in the stream of complaints.] Lull designates an interval of stillness or calm that contrasts with prior and subsequent noise or confusion: a lull in a storm. Lull may also refer to a falling off of activity, implying a loss of momentum and suggesting the sluggishness of a slack period: a lull in business; a lull in the conversation.

Let-up 是一个非正式用词，通常在 no 或 without 之后使用，通常表示减弱而不是停止，表示力量的减弱、速度的放慢或数量或强度的减少。停顿；我们已经工作了两个小时，没有停顿；抱怨的声音没有停歇。风暴也可能指活动的减少，暗示动力的丧失，并暗示淡季的低迷：生意的平静；谈话的平静。


4.91 Bleak
These words refer to people or things that look wasted or inhospitable. Bleak is the most general of these and can apply equally well to people or things, especially landscapes or houses. It suggests a bare or unpleasant prospect: the bleak, ice-encrusted mountains of the Andes; the bleak, unpainted house that seemed almost uninhabitable. Used of people, it suggests a facial expression that is unhappy or unfriendly: She gave her husband a bleak, unsatisfied look. It can, of course, suggest anything unhopeful or unpromising: their one bleak hope for survival.

这些词指的是看起来荒凉或荒凉的人或事物，它同样适用于人或事物，尤其是风景或房屋，它暗示着一种光秃秃的或不愉快的前景：荒凉、冰雪覆盖的山脉。安第斯山脉的荒凉、未粉刷的房子似乎几乎无法居住，它暗示着不高兴或不友好的面部表情：当然，它可以暗示任何不希望或没有希望的表情。 ：他们生存的唯一希望。

Gaunt and haggard are more closely tied to the physical appearance of people. Gaunt stresses leanness but it may or may not suggest a wasted or shrunken appearance: the sailor’s gaunt, weather-beaten face. Haggard, however, insists on emaciation or at very least suggests a drawn expression resulting from strain or shock: the haggard faces of the prisoners in the concentration camp; a face haggard with grief. Gaunt can also apply to things or landscapes, in which case it suggests a harsh or bare scene: the gaunt moors of the Brontë country. In this context, bleak is more intense than gaunt: grateful for even the gaunt plains after the bleak wasteland of the desert. Haggard would sound less natural in describing anything other than people, but used metaphorically, it might suggest a worn, run-down appearance: the rows of haggard houses that testified to poverty and neglect.

憔悴和憔悴与人们的外貌关系更密切，但它可能会也可能不会暗示一种消瘦或萎缩的外观：然而，水手的憔悴、饱经风霜的脸却坚持憔悴或至少是憔悴的。表示由于紧张或震惊而造成的紧张表情：集中营中囚犯的憔悴面孔；憔悴的表情也可以适用于事物或风景，在这种情况下，它表示严酷或光秃秃的场景：憔悴的荒原。在勃朗特国家的背景下，“荒凉”比“荒凉”更强烈：在描述荒凉的沙漠荒原之后，即使是对荒凉的平原表示感激，在描述除了人之外的任何事物时，它可能会显得不太自然。破旧、破败的外观：一排排因贫困和忽视而苦恼的破旧房屋。

Desolate and barren refer to uninhabitable or unfeatured landscape. Desolate suggests an underpopulated starkness, barren a complete absence of life: only a few farmhouses strung out over the desolate countryside; barren rocks where the smallest shrub could find no foothold. Desolate can, however, also suggest solitariness or friendlessness: a desolate pine or two struggling for life above the timber line: a girl left desolate in the strange city. Barren, like bleak, can suggest an unpromising outlook; a plan barren of practical remedies. Barren, in the sense discussed here, could not be applied to people.

荒凉和贫瘠指的是不适合居住或没有特色的景观，荒凉，荒凉，完全没有生命：荒凉的乡村中只有几座农舍；荒凉的岩石上最小的灌木也找不到立足点。也暗示孤独或无朋友：一两棵荒凉的松树在木材线上方挣扎：一个女孩被遗弃在陌生的城市，就像荒凉一样，可以暗示一个没有任何实际补救措施的计划。这里讨论的意义，不能应用于人。

SEE: DISMAL, GLOOMY
	ANTONYMS: CHEERFUL, COMFORTABLE, HEALTHY, luxurious.
	
	
4.92 Blithe
These words refer to a pleasant, warm, cheerful or high-spirited	disposition or manner. Blithe indicates an attitude that is cheerful,mirthful, joyous or gay: blithe crowds enjoying the sunny weather in the park. The word can have a less favourable application to a manner that is casual, indifferent or airy, particularly when directed towards something that should be taken seriously: listening to my grievance with a blithe lack of concern.	

这些词指的是令人愉快的、热情的、开朗的或昂扬的性格或举止。 Blithe 表示一种开朗、快乐、快乐或快乐的态度：愉快的人群在公园里享受阳光明媚的天气。以一种随意、冷漠或轻率的方式，特别是当针对应该认真对待的事情时：以一种无忧无虑、漠不关心的态度倾听我的不满。

Genial points to a more low-key or long-term good-humoured attitude that is exhibited in a kindly, pleasant or warm manner; it suggests an unruffled or even temper and an ability to put people at ease: an extremely genial host. Light-hearted is closer in tone to blithe, since it suggests an absence of care or a positive state of buoyant delight: light-hearted youngsters singing as the hiked through the bush. A contrast of how one feels, whereas the very essence of light-hearted is its suggestion of a spontaneous welling up of high spirits. Genial, furthermore, suggests friendly relationships with others; light-hearted may pertain to someone completely alone.

和蔼是指一种比较低调或长期幽默的态度，以一种和善、愉快或温暖的方式表现出来；它表示一种不慌不忙甚至脾气暴躁、能让人放松的能力：一个极其和蔼可亲的主人。 -heart 的语气更接近 blithe，因为它暗示着一种无忧无虑的状态或一种积极的快乐状态：轻松愉快的年轻人在徒步穿过灌木丛时唱歌，与一个人的感受形成鲜明对比，而 light 的本质是——愉快的暗示着自发的兴高采烈，此外，愉快的暗示可能与完全孤独的人有关。

Convivial serves as an intensification of genial, suggesting jolly sociability and warm fellow-feeling; its Latin root pertains to a feast or banquet and this is often reflected in the English use of the word: convivial merrymakers at the carnival. Jovial may suggest sociability, but it is less specific in indicating any sort of good-natured amiability. The word is very often used to describe a jolly but dignified fat man, so much so that the word is sometimes taken to specify this situation. Similarly, blithe sometimes suggests a spry, elfin or fey person, particularly a woman.

Convivial 是 genial 的强化，暗示快乐的社交和温暖的同胞感觉；它的拉丁词根与盛宴或宴会有关，这通常反映在该词的英语用法中：convivial merrymakers at the carnival 可能暗示社交，但它不太具体地表示任何种类的善良和蔼可亲，这个词经常被用来描述一个快乐但有尊严的胖子，以至于有时这个词被用来指定这种情况。敏捷、精灵或怪异的人，尤其是女人。

Elated an ebullient both refer, like light-hearted, to a welling up of high spirits. Elated, however, can often refer to a response to some external occurrence or news, whereas ebullient suggests the same spontaneity as light-hearted. Ebullient stems from the root of a Latin word meaning to boil out, and the English word reflects this in pointing to a bubbling over with enthusiasm, excitement or exuberance: fans who were elated when the team scored another goal; an ebullient personality that always seemed to overflow with vivacity and zest.

兴高采烈和热情洋溢一样，都指兴高采烈，然而，兴高采烈通常可以指对某些外部事件或新闻的反应，而热情洋溢则表示与轻松愉快的根源相同的自发性。拉丁语中的单词意为“沸腾”，英语单词则反映了热情、兴奋或热情的沸腾：当球队再次进球时兴高采烈的球迷；热情洋溢的个性，似乎总是洋溢着活力和热情。 。

SEE: PLEASURE.
	ANTONYMS: DISMAL, GLOOMY, ill-humoured, melancholic, morose, SAD, sullen, TRANQUIL.


4.93 Blockhead
These words are all informal pejoratives for people who behave in stupid or foolish ways. Blockhead, dolt and dunce suggest foolish behaviour that results from a lack of intelligence. Blockhead suggests a dense, slow-witted person who predictably misunderstands information or is filled with exasperatingly obvious ideas or attitudes: a party at which he talked with one insufferable blockhead after another. Dolt specifically suggests a lack of flair, imagination or perception that results from cloddish conventionality: dolts in the audience who liked her medley of show-tunes better than her group of Schubert songs. Dunce may suggest a momentary failure of intelligence rather than a permanent lack of it: He made a dunce of himself by forgetting the name of the guest of honour.

这些词都是对行为愚蠢的人的非正式贬义词，“傻瓜”和“傻瓜”表示由于缺乏智力而做出的愚蠢行为。明显的想法或态度：在一次聚会上，他与一个又一个令人难以忍受的傻瓜交谈，特别表明了由于粗俗的传统而缺乏天赋、想象力或感知力：观众中的傻瓜比她更喜欢她的表演曲调。邓斯的一组舒伯特歌曲可能暗示着智力的暂时失败，而不是永久的缺乏：他忘记了主宾的名字，从而自取其辱。

Fool, idiot and chump need not suggest a lack of intelligence. All can suggest silly or ridiculous behaviour that arises from any number of causes: letting the woman make a fool of him; don’t be an idiot ?accept the offer of a new job. Chump, besides being a much more informal substitute for fool, can indicate somebody who allows himself to be come the butt of a joke or confidence game: looking for chumps who could be lured into buying worthless share certificates. Chump can also be a severely contemptuous term for any sort of unsophiscated or ordinary person: chumps dumb enough to be taken in by sensational journalism. Like a chump or a fool, a dill is easily taken in or can usually be relied on to do the stupid or naive thing: a bit of a dill, the way he always lets others take advantage of him.

“傻瓜”、“白痴”和“笨蛋”并不意味着缺乏智慧，所有这些都可以暗示由多种原因引起的愚蠢或可笑的行为：让女人愚弄他，不要成为白痴？接受新的提议。 “Cump”除了是“傻瓜”的更非正式的替代品之外，还可以表示一个让自己成为笑话或信任游戏的笑柄的人：寻找可能被引诱购买毫无价值股票的傻瓜也可以是一个“傻瓜”。对任何不成熟或普通人的严重蔑视的术语：愚蠢到被耸人听闻的新闻所欺骗的人，像傻瓜或傻瓜一样，很容易被欺骗或通常可以依靠做愚蠢或天真的事情：有点莳萝，他总是让别人利用他。

The remaining group of words relates to the last suggestion of chump and dill in indicating contempt for ordinary or simple people. When it is not an informal substitute for fool, boob suggests a heavy, stupid person. Nincompoop has particular relevance in describing a foolish man, suggesting a weakling afflicted by timidity and passivity: situation comedies that stereotype husbands as bumbling nincompoops. Ninny can apply to either sex, but may be particularly useful in reference to foolish women, suggesting silly, precious or prissy behaviour: a ninny who wrote saccharine poems about butterflies and daffodils.

剩下的一组词与最后一个词“chump”和“dill”有关，表示对普通人或简单人的蔑视。当它不是“傻瓜”的非正式替代品时，“boob”表示“笨重的、愚蠢的人”，在描述一个愚蠢的人时特别相关。 ，暗示受胆怯和被动折磨的弱者：将丈夫刻板印象为笨手笨脚的傻瓜的情景喜剧可以适用于任何性别，但可能对愚蠢的女性特别有用，暗示愚蠢，珍贵或拘谨的行为：一个写糖精的傻瓜。关于蝴蝶和水仙花的诗。

SEE: MORON.
	ANTONYMS: sage, savant, wise man.


4.94 Bloody
These words refer to the spilling of blood or to an attitude that delights in bloodshed. Bloody suggests freshly spilt blood or conflict that results in heavy casualties: the bloody hands of the suspect; the bloody, four-day battle. It is also frequently used as an epithet for someone or something responsible for wanton slaughter: the bloody Stalinist purges; Hitler’s bloody henchmen; Bloody Mary. Bloody has come to be used as a curse word for anything displeasing. This use was once taken as a blasphemous reference to Christ’s blood, but over-use has weakened its force: He cursed the bloody tricycle he had tripped over in the dark. Gory, by contrast, suggests clotted or dried blood: police photographing the gory knife. It may also refer to any production that revels in giving extremely detailed accounts of gruesome accidents or murders: a gory detective story. This use also appears in the cliché, the gory details, which suggests the loving and minute description of anything unpleasant.

这些词指的是流血或以流血为乐的态度，血腥意味着新鲜的流血或造成重大伤亡的冲突：嫌疑人的血淋淋的双手；血腥的、持续四天的战斗。作为对肆意屠杀的某人或某物的绰号：血腥的斯大林主义清洗；血腥玛丽已被用作任何令人不快的事物的咒语。 ，但过度使用削弱了它的力量：相比之下，他诅咒了他在黑暗中绊倒的血淋淋的三轮车，血腥意味着凝结或干涸的血液：警察拍摄的血腥刀也可能指任何陶醉于其中的作品。对可怕的事故或谋杀进行极其详细的描述：血腥的侦探故事也出现在陈词滥调中，血腥的细节，暗示对任何不愉快的事情的爱和细致的描述。

The remaining words apply primarily to an eagerness to let blood, either literally or figuratively. Bloodthirsty is most specific here, suggesting a delight in inflicting harm on others, especially in armed combat: bloodthirsty generals who urged the king to declare war; bloodthirsty guerillas intent on terrorizing the native villagers. The word can also be used figuratively to describe people who enjoy reading or seeing accounts of bloody happenings: bloodthirsty audiences who dote on gory television dramas.

其余的词主要适用于渴望流血，无论是字面意思还是比喻意义上的嗜血在这里最为具体，暗示着对他人造成伤害的快乐，尤其是在武装战斗中：嗜血的将军敦促国王宣战，嗜血的游击队意图。这个词也可以用来比喻那些喜欢阅读或观看血腥事件的人：喜爱血腥电视剧的嗜血观众。

Sanguinary is considerably more formal than these other words, giving a literary, almost euphemistic substitute for bloody or bloodthirsty: the sanguinary oppression of the conquered nation. It may also be used merely to refer to someone in a foul temper or ugly frame of mind: a sanguinary disposition.

血腥比这些其他词要正式得多，它是血腥或嗜血的文学，几乎是委婉的替代品：被​​征服国家的血腥压迫它也可以仅用来指脾气暴躁或思想丑陋的人：嗜血的性格

SEE: GRUESOME.
	ANTONYMS: bloodless, HUMANE, merciful.
	
	
4.95 Blow
These nouns denote various ways of hitting with the hand. Blow is the inclusive term. In a generic sense, it may be applied to any forceful impact of a hand, implement, or weapon against another object: a blow with the flat of the hand; a hammer blow; a blow with a blunt object. In specific comparison with the other words, a blow is a forceful hit with the fist: The fighter felled his opponent with a mighty blow. Punch is a more informal word than blow; and, unlike blow, it is limited in application. A punch is a quick, short blow or jab with the fist, typically aimed at a particular target: a punch in the eye. Punch is a boxing term: to throw a punch; to land a punch; to roll with a punch. A boxer dazed by repeated blows to the head is referred to as punch-drunk. Outside the ring, punch often suggests a belligerent attitude, the desire to pick a fight: I’m going to give you a punch in the nose.

这些名词表示用手击打的各种方式，从一般意义上讲，它可以应用于手、工具或武器对另一个物体的任何强力冲击：用手掌击打。 ; 锤击；用钝器击打 与其他词相比，击打是用拳头强力击打：拳击手用强力击打击打是一个比击打更非正式的词。与击打不同，拳头是用拳头快速、短促地击打或刺击，通常针对特定目标：拳打在眼睛上是一个拳击术语：用拳头击打目标。拳头；拳击手因反复击打头部而晕眩，在拳击场外，拳头通常表示好战的态度，即挑衅的欲望：我要投降。你打鼻子。

A slap is a sharp blow delivered with the open hand or with something flat. A slap in the face stings or smarts and is often intended to be a rebuke; Her date started to get fresh and she gave him a slap. In earlier days, a slap on the cheek with a glove was a calculated insult whereby one man challenged another to a duel. But a slap in the face may be given to shock someone out of hysteria. And a slap on the back is a hearty, friendly, man-to-man form of greeting or congratulations.

打耳光是用张开的手或用扁平的东西猛烈地打在脸上，通常是为了责备；她的约会对象开始变得新鲜，她打了他一巴掌。用手套打脸是一种蓄意的侮辱，因此一个人向另一个人发起决斗，但打脸可以让某人从歇斯底里中惊醒，而打背则是一个热心、友善的人。 - 对人的问候或祝贺。

Cuff once could mean a blow with the fist, a usage that survives in the word fisticuffs; but now a cuff is usually a sidelong blow with the open hand or a cushioned slap with a paw: The mother cat gave her kitten a cuff. A box may be struck with the palm or fist, but where cuff stresses the type of blow, box emphasizes the part of the body that is hit ?the ear, cheek or side of the head. Both box and cuff are specifically applied to a slap on the ear, a punishment that was part of the schoolhouse discipline of an earlier era: to give an unruly boy a cuff (or a box) on the ear.
	
Cuff 曾经意味着用拳头击打，这种用法在“拳头”一词中得以保留；但现在，“cuff”通常是张开的手侧击或用爪子拍打：母猫给了她的小猫一个“A”拳头。 box 可以用手掌或拳头击打，但 cuff 强调击打的类型，box 强调击打的身体部位 - 耳朵、脸颊或头部侧面。 box 和 cuff 都专门适用于打耳光。打耳朵，这是早期校舍纪律的一部分的惩罚：给不守规矩的男孩打耳朵上的手铐（或盒子）。

A rap is a sharp, quick blow and a knock is a harder, heavier one. Both may be made with the knuckles, and both make sounds that signal a person’s presence: an insistent knock at the door; a light rap on the window pane. But a rap may also be administered with an implement as a mild form of punishment, and in this case the knuckles may receive the blow rather than striking it: The teacher gave him a rap on the knuckles with her ruler. Figuratively, to take the rap is to accept punishment for some failure or misdeed. Knock as a noun suggests the physical punishment of a fight only in a figurative sense: the school of hard knocks. In a similar way, to take the knock is to be hard hit or responsible financially. Blow, punch, and slap are also used figuratively. A slap in the face is an insult, rebuke or slur. An editorial with punch has vitality and force. A blow is a calamity that hits the emotions with a sudden, forceful impact: His tragic death was a blow from which she never fully recovered.

敲击声是一种尖锐、快速的敲击声，而敲击声则是一种更用力、更重的敲击声，两者都可以用指关节发出，并且都会发出表明有人在场的声音：持续不断地敲门；敲击窗玻璃。但敲击也可以作为一种温和的惩罚形式，在这种情况下，指关节可能会受到打击而不是击打：老师用她的尺子敲击了他的指关节，以接受。 rap 是接受对某些失败或不当行为的惩罚，作为名词，仅在比喻意义上暗示打架的体罚：类似地，接受敲击是指受到重击或重击。打击、拳头和耳光也被用作比喻。 打耳光是一种侮辱、斥责或诽谤。 带有拳头的社论具有活力和力量，是一种突然而有力的打击情绪的灾难。影响：他的悲惨死亡对她来说是一个沉重的打击，她从未完全康复。

SEE: BEAT, FIGHT.
	ANTONYMS: caress, touch.
	
	
4.96 Blush
All these words have uses to describe the change in a person’s facial appearance when he is embarrassed or under a strain. Blush is specifically restricted to the rushing of blood into the face of someone who is shocked or embarrassed: She blushed easily at any talk of bodily functions. It is more commonly used to describe a woman; a man who blushes might be thought effeminate. Colour is a less precise, almost euphemistic synonym for blush: the girl who coloured under his glance. When applied to a man, it might suggest an attempt to avoid the effeminacy implied in blush. In any case, because colour has so many other uses and can sound confusing in this context, it might best be avoided altogether.
	
所有这些词都用来描述一个人在感到尴尬或紧张时面部表情的变化。“脸红”专门限于震惊或尴尬的人脸上的血液涌上来：她在任何谈话中都很容易脸红。它更常用于形容女人；脸红的男人可能被认为是女性化的。颜色是脸红的一个不那么精确、几乎是委婉的同义词：当应用于男人时，它可能会被认为是女性。建议尝试避免腮红所暗示的女性化。无论如何，因为颜色有很多其他用途，并且在这种情况下听起来可能令人困惑，所以最好完全避免。

Flush, like colour, might be used in place of blush to avoid any note of effeminacy: his face flushing at the mere mention of her name. It is more commonly used, however, to refer to a feverish condition, either from illness, exertion or exposure: their faces flushed from hours of drill and callisthenics. Flush can also indicate emotional seizures other than embarrassment: a face flushed with anger; a crowd flushed with excitement.

Flush 和 color 一样，可以用来代替 blush，以避免任何女性化的感觉：他的脸一听到她的名字就泛红，然而，更常用的是指因疾病或劳累而发烧的情况。或暴露：他们的脸因数小时的训练和健美操而变红，这也可能表明除了尴尬之外的情绪发作：脸因愤怒而涨红；人群因兴奋而涨红。

Redden, like colour, can substitute for blush, but in being specific about the physical change involved, it sounds less euphemistic than colour. It also, like flush, can result from other emotional seizures: a scowl reddened by rage. Both redden and colour can, of course, describe skin changes outside the present context: a face reddened by long exposure to sun and wind; the skin slowly colouring from the sharp blow.

红色，像颜色一样，可以代替脸红，但具体到所涉及的身体变化，它听起来不像颜色那么委婉。它也像脸红一样，可能是由其他情绪发作引起的：因愤怒而变红的皱眉。当然，可以描述当前环境之外的皮肤变化：由于长时间暴露在阳光和风中而变红的脸；由于猛烈的打击而慢慢变色的皮肤。

SEE: COLOUR.
	ANTONYMS: blanch, PALE, whiten.
	

4.97 Boast
These words refer to feelings of self-congratulation. Boast may suggest justifiable self-satisfaction: a college that boasts an unusually high number of distinguished Old Boys. More often, however, the word suggests a self-important and tasteless pointing out of one’s own successes: He monopolized the conversation by boasting of his own prowess at hunting and fishing; continually boasting and blowing his own horn. Occasionally the word can refer to self-congratulation for a victory not yet won: He boasted that he would finish off the challenger in the first round. Pride is close to the justified self-satisfaction possible for boast, but it more often specifically suggests private self-regard rather than a public expression of it; it is usually reflexive: He secretly prided himself on a life of absolute honesty. The word can suggest a stiff-necked self-righteousness or a faulty estimate of one’s own virtues: Priding himself on his democratic outlook, he nevertheless sent his children to a private school.
	
这些词指的是自我庆幸的感觉，可能暗示着一种合理的自我满足：一所拥有异常多的杰出老男孩的大学，然而，这个词更多的时候暗示着一种自以为是和无品味的指出。成功：他通过吹嘘自己在狩猎和钓鱼方面的能力来垄断谈话；不断地吹嘘和吹响自己的号角，这个词有时可以指对尚未赢得的胜利的自我庆贺：他吹嘘他会消灭挑战者。在第一轮中，骄傲接近于夸耀时可能出现的合理的自我满足，但它更经常地表明私人的自尊，而不是公开的表达；它通常是反射性的：他暗自为自己的绝对生活感到自豪。诚实这个词可能意味着顽固的自以为是或对自己美德的错误估计：他对自己的民主观点感到自豪，但还是把孩子送到了私立学校。

Brag intensifies the note of tastelessness in boast, suggesting limitless conceit and, possibly, inaccuracy of the claims being made: bragging about his imaginary exploits in the last war; bragging about his son’s success at school as a way of patting himself on the back. Crow suggests noisy or vociferous bragging of an extremely offensive kind after the event: publicly crowing about the defeat of his opponent. Gloat is an intensification of crow. Although it need not be verbal and sometimes suggests taunting someone that one has bested: rubbing his hands in secret and gloating over the way he had made the other applicants look foolish; gloating openly and lording it over those who had failed the examination.

吹牛强化了吹嘘中的无趣，暗示了无限的自负，而且可能还存在不准确的说法：吹嘘他在上次战争中想象中的功绩；吹嘘他儿子在学校的成功，以此作为一种自我表扬的方式。乌鸦暗示在比赛结束后进行一种极其无礼的大声吹嘘：公开吹嘘对手的失败是乌鸦的一种强化，尽管它不一定是口头的，有时还暗示着嘲笑被击败的人：搓手。暗中幸灾乐祸，让其他申请者显得愚蠢；公开幸灾乐祸，对那些考试不及格的人发号施令。

Strut suggests less animus than gloat but it is similar in not necessarily being verbal. It invariably suggests, however, an act done as a matter of public display: so puffed up and smug over his recent successes that he could not refrain from strutting about and preening himself before his fewer and fewer friends. Vaunt is considerably more formal than the other words here; it compares to the understandable self-satisfaction suggested by boast, but it is a shade more self-righteous, possibly suggesting a claim that cannot be substantiated. It differs from pride in usually implying a public expression of self-esteem: vaunting far and wide the cultural opportunities lying in wait for visitors to their small town.

斯特鲁特所暗示的不是敌意，而是幸灾乐祸，但它不一定是口头上的，但它总是暗示着一种公开展示的行为：对他最近的成功如此自负和沾沾自喜，以至于他无法克制地趾高气扬。在他越来越少的朋友面前炫耀自己比这里的其他词要正式得多，与夸耀所暗示的可以理解的自我满足相比，它更自以为是，可能暗示着一种无法证实的主张。它与骄傲不同，通常意味着公开表达自尊：到处炫耀等待游客来到小镇的文化机会。

SEE: CONCEITED, CONFIDENCE, EGOISM.
	ANTONYMS: BELITTLE, minimize, underrate.
	

4.98 Boil
These words all refer to methods of cooking by direct heat or flame, especially on to of a stove. Boil implies rapid cooking in more or less large quantities of water heated to the point (212° at sea level) where bubbles escape at the surface: to boil potatoes; to boil an egg.
	
这些词都是指通过直接加热或火焰进行烹饪的方法，尤其是在炉子上煮沸意味着在或多或少的大量水中快速烹饪，加热到气泡从表面逸出的程度（海平面212°）。 ：煮土豆；煮鸡蛋。

Simmer means to cook slowly in a hot liquid just below the boiling point, and usually for a long time.	

慢煮是指在略低于沸点的热液体中慢慢煮，通常要煮很长时间。

To steam food is to cook it by direct exposure to steam or by using heat generated by steam, as in a double boiler. Direct steaming is usually accomplished by placing a metal rack above the level of shallow boiling water in a pot so that the food does not touch the water: to steam fish; to steam vegetables. Poach implies a method of cooking a few foods, such as eggs without their shells, or pieces of chicken or fish, by dropping them into hot water, milk or stock and simmering until done.

蒸食物是通过直接暴露在蒸汽中或利用蒸汽产生的热量来烹饪食物，如在双层锅炉中，直接蒸通常是通过将金属架放置在锅中浅沸水的水平上方来完成的。不接触水：蒸鱼；蒸蔬菜是指将一些食物（例如去壳的鸡蛋、鸡肉或鱼块）放入热水、牛奶或高汤中煮沸的方法。直到完成。

Stew is a close synonym of simmer in that both mean to cook slowly in liquid over low heat; to stew prunes. However, to most people, stew strongly suggests the familiar dish that is cooked in this way -- meat combined with vegetables in a gravy or sauce. Stewing always involves simmering, but one may simmer (not stew) soups, vegetables, sauces, etc.

Stew 是 simmer 的近义词，因为两者都意味着用小火在液体中慢慢煮；然而，对于大多数人来说，stew 强烈暗示以这种方式烹饪的熟悉菜肴 - 将肉与蔬菜放在一起。肉汁或酱汁总是需要煨，但也可以煨（而不是炖）汤、蔬菜、酱汁等。

When cooks speak of stewing meat, they usually mean to braise it. Braise implies the browning of meat (and often of accompanying vegetables) in a small amount of fat prior to adding a stock or other liquid and simmering in a covered pan.

当厨师谈到炖肉时，他们通常指的是炖，即在加入高汤或其他液体并在有盖的平底锅中慢炖之前，将肉（通常还有伴随的蔬菜）煎成褐色。

Fry and sauté are closely related in that the food is cooked in hot fat. Sautéing, is done very quickly with a minimum amount of fat and may or may not imply browning. Meat is usually sautéed before it is braised. Frying suggests cooking in greater amounts of fat than that used in sautéing, and may be done in a pan containing up to one or two inches of fat or in a pot designed for deep frying, in which large amounts of fat are used. Dry-frying is the complete cooking of meat (chops, steak, etc.) by frying slowly in little or no fat. Foods, especially potatoes, cooked in deep fat until crisp are often called "French-fried."

煎和炒的密切相关之处在于，食物是用热油烹制的，用最少的脂肪很快就能完成，并且可能会或可能不会意味着肉在炖之前先煎一下。比煎炸中使用的脂肪量要多，并且可以在含有最多一或两英寸脂肪的平底锅中进行，或者在专为油炸而设计的锅中进行，其中使用大量的脂肪干煎是完整的烹饪。将肉（排骨、牛排等）在很少或没有脂肪的情况下慢慢煎炸 食物，尤其是土豆，在深油中烹制至酥脆，通常称为“法式油炸”。

One pot-roasts a large piece of meat by placing it in a little fat in a large saucepan on top of the stove, so that it cooks slowly, perhaps surrounded by roasting vegetables.

锅烤法是将一大块肉放入炉子顶部的大平底锅中，放入少许脂肪，慢慢地煮，周围可能还放着烤蔬菜。

SEE: GRILL.


4.99 Bold
These words share the connotation of self-assertive, confident and energetic dispositions, with or without a disregard for the rights of others. Bold shares with aggressive the implication of a vigorous attack on a problem or prosecution of one’s aims, and in this sense carries no derogatory connotation. An aggressive or bold entrepreneur will seek success farther afield and will risk more in this search than will his more timid competitor. Bold does, however, have a wider ranges of application than aggressive. In some contexts bold suggests impudence or cheekiness, although this use is certainly less common now than it once was: The bold fellow simply put out his hand and asked for more money. In other contexts it suggests commendable enterprise: a bold new venture in space science. Aggressive typically describes one who has a more lively sense of his own destiny than of other people’s feelings.

这些词都蕴含着自信、自信和精力充沛的性格，不管是否忽视他人的权利，“大胆”都含有积极攻击某个问题或追求自己目标的含义，从这个意义上讲，它具有积极进取的含义。没有贬义。 一个激进或大胆的企业家会比他胆小的竞争对手更远地寻求成功，但在某些情况下，“大胆”一词的应用范围更广。 ，尽管这种用法现在肯定不像以前那么常见了：大胆的家伙只是伸出手来要求更多的钱。在其他情况下，它暗示着值得称赞的事业：太空科学领域的大胆新冒险通常描述了一个人。对自己的命运比对其他人的感受有更强烈的认识。

Aggressive shares with forward and pushing a derogatory connotation of callousness in seeking one’s ends. A forward or pushing social climber may resort to gossip, slander and back-biting. Pushing may also be used in the less derogatory sense of aggressive to mean enterprising and energetic.

Aggressive 与forward 和 Pushing 具有贬义含义，表示在寻求自己的手段时冷酷无情。 一个前锋或推动的社交攀登者可能会说闲话、诽谤和中伤他人，Pushing 也可以用在不太贬义的意义上，表示积极进取和精力充沛。 。

SEE: OPPORTUNISTIC, RECKLESS.
	ANTONYMS: AFRAID, COWARDLY, MODEST, TIMID.
	
	
4.100 Bombastic
These words are used to describe styles of speaking or writing. Bombastic and turgid are alike in designating a lack of restraint and discipline that so inflates the language used in a piece of writing or in a speech that its style and content are thrown out of balance. Bombastic is derived from the noun bombast which originally denoted the kind of cotton, wool or other soft material which is used for padding and stuffing. The suggestion of padding is very much present in any reference to a bombastic style which, though it does not always connote the complete absence of thought, certainly indicates an imbalance between the thought and the manner used to express it: For so trivial a topic, his speech was bombastic and cheaply theatrical. Turgid literally means swollen or distended, as by contained air or liquid: a healthy, turgid muscle; a leg turgid with infection. Like bombastic, turgid carries over a suggestion of its literal meaning into its figurative reference to style: a tiny idea which the author has blown up into this turgid, trying novel. Orotund is used positively to describe a full, clear, round and resonant tone of voice. The figurative sense of the word, however, is pejorative in its synonymity with bombastic. Orotund can apply to pompous, inflated speech or writing, but, because of its particular reference to sound, it is most often used to describe the spoken word: a speech so orotund as to cause yawns and whispers all over the auditorium. Purple, in the sense being compared here, means ornate or flowery. It is pejorative in its suggestion of too much colour and showiness: a good playwright who ruined some of his most dramatic moments with passages of bad poetry and purple prose. It also has come to refer to the erotic, the lurid, the vulgar or the profane: a TV compere whose interviews led to such purple exchanges that a sponsor demanded his dismissal.

这些词用来描述说话或写作的风格，它们都表示缺乏克制和纪律，以致文章或演讲中使用的语言过于夸张，以致其风格和内容失去平衡。 Bombastic 源自名词“bombast”，最初表示用于填充物和填充物的棉、羊毛或其他柔软材料。任何提及“夸张”风格的地方都经常出现填充物的暗示，尽管并不总是如此。意味着完全没有思想，当然表明了思想和表达它的方式之间的不平衡：对于如此琐碎的话题，他的演讲是夸夸其谈和廉价的戏剧性，“Turgid”字面意思是肿胀或膨胀，就像通过包含的空气或液体一样：健康、肿胀的肌肉；感染而肿胀的腿部。 就像夸夸其谈一样，“肿胀”将其字面意义带入了其对风格的比喻：作者在这部肿胀、尝试的小说中使用了一个微小的想法。积极地描述一种完整、清晰、圆润和洪亮的语气，然而，这个词的比喻意义是贬义的，它与夸夸其谈的同义词可以适用于浮夸、夸大的演讲或写作，但是，因为它的特殊指称。就声音而言，它最常用于描述口语：演讲声音如此响亮，以致在礼堂里引起哈欠和窃窃私语，在这里所比较的含义是华丽的或华丽的，它是贬义的。过多的色彩和浮夸：一位优秀的剧作家，用糟糕的诗歌和紫色散文毁掉了他最戏剧性的时刻。导致了如此紫色的交易，以至于赞助商要求解雇他。


4.101 Bony
These adjectives refer to extreme thinness in which the underlying bones are evident. Bony is the most general word and is relatively free of connotations. It simply indicates a prominent bone structure, whether this is deemed a sign of attractiveness, asceticism, chronic undernourishment or near-starvation: a crooner’s bony, boyish face; a waif-like actress with bony shoulders and big eyes; a bony Indian fakir; a bony, sway-backed nag. Bony is frequently applied to a single part of the body: long, bony fingers; bony knees. And it may sometimes emphasize attributes of bone that are not seen but felt, such as hardness or sharpness: She jabbed me with a bony elbow.
	
这些形容词指的是极度瘦弱，骨瘦如柴，是最通用的词，相对没有任何含义，它只是表示突出的骨骼结构，无论这是否被视为吸引力、禁欲主义、长期营养不良的标志。 -饥饿：歌手骨瘦如柴、孩子气的脸；瘦骨嶙峋的肩膀和大眼睛的流浪者；瘦骨嶙峋的印度苦行僧；瘦骨嶙峋的马驹经常出现在身体的某个部位：又长又瘦。有时，它可能会强调看不见但摸得着的骨头属性，例如硬度或锋利度：她用骨头肘部戳我。

Gaunt implies a paucity of flesh and prominence of bone. It comes from the Old Norse word for a tall, thin person and it indicates an angular leanness: the tall, gaunt figure of Don Quixote. Specifically, gaunt often calls to mind the haggard look of the hungry, anguished, ill or old. It suggests the weariness of long suffering or constant strain, describing one who seems to have been worn down to the bone: the gaunt, ascetic figure of a saint; a gaunt old man, hollow-eyed, with prominent cheekbones and attenuated limbs.

憔悴的意思是肌肉缺乏、骨骼突出，这个词源自古挪威语，意为高瘦的人，表示有棱有角的瘦削：具体来说，憔悴的形象常常让人想起憔悴的样子。它暗示着饥饿、痛苦、生病或年老的人的疲倦，形容一个人似乎已经疲惫不堪：一个憔悴的、苦行僧般的圣人形象；有眼睛，颧骨突出，四肢削薄。

Wasted implies a loss of flesh, stressing the cause of bony thinness. A wasted body is one that has been gradually consumed ?reduced to skin and bone by the ravages of time, grief, hunger or disease: wasted away by tuberculosis; a pallid face and wasted frame. Hence wasted implies physical weakness and frailty; the wasted form of a 100-year-old woman; a body wasted by disease.

消瘦意味着肌肉的流失，强调了骨骼瘦弱的原因，消瘦的身体是由于时间、悲伤、饥饿或疾病的蹂躏而逐渐消耗殆尽的身体：因肺结核而消瘦；因苍白的脸而消瘦。因此，“衰弱”意味着身体虚弱；百岁妇女的身体因疾病而衰弱。

Emaciated focuses on both the cause and the fact of abnormal leanness. It indicates a previous wasting away, implying the depletion of the body by grave illness, great suffering or terrible deprivation. Skeletal is the most extreme of all these words, pointing to the deathlike dominance of bone. Both skeletal and emaciated may suggest the leanness of living men who look like skeletons, their ribs and sharp bones showing through the skin: emaciated (or skeletal) survivors of a Nazi concentration camp. But skeletal has about it the further suggestion of something lifeless of unreal, not fully human or alive: a painting of skeletal men and women in a barren future world; a novelist whose characters seem to be skeletal symbols, thoroughly analysed but not fleshed out and never really brought to life. Emaciated, by contrast, is often expressive of human pity or horror at a skeletal appearance: the awful sight of emaciated children with distended bellies and glazed expressions.

“憔悴”既强调异常消瘦的原因，也强调其事实。它表示先前的消瘦，暗示身体因严重疾病、巨大痛苦或可怕的匮乏而耗尽。“骨骼”是所有这些词中最极端的，指的是死亡般的情况。骨骼占主导地位。 骨骼和瘦骨嶙峋都可能暗示着活生生的人看起来像骷髅，他们的肋骨和锋利的骨头透过皮肤显现出来：纳粹集中营的瘦弱（或骨骼）幸存者，但骨骼有进一步的暗示。一些没有生命的虚幻的东西，不完全是人性的或有生命的：一幅贫瘠的未来世界中骷髅男女的画作；一位小说家的人物似乎是骷髅符号，经过彻底的分析，但没有充实起来，也从未真正被赋予生命。相比之下，它通常表达人类对骨骼外观的怜悯或恐惧：瘦弱的儿童，腹部遥远，表情呆滞的可怕景象。

SEE: LANKY, PALE, THIN, WEAKEN.
	ANTONYMS: FAT, nourished, well-fed.
	
	
4.102 Boss
These words all refer to persons who are in authority over others. Boss is a colloquial word that originated in the United States and in its strictest sense applies to an employer, foreman or manger of a group of workmen. By extension it has also become a popular term for any executive, supervisor or immediate superior: the boss of a large clothing store. Boss may also apply to any person who is in control of things, whether by prerogative or by tyrannical behaviour. [A horse must understand who is boss; Many parents discover that a spoilt child has become boss of the household.]

这些词都指的是对他人有权威的人。 Boss 是一个起源于美国的口语词，严格意义上适用于一群工人的雇主、工头或经理。任何主管、主管或直接上级的通俗术语：大型服装店的老板也适用于任何控制事物的人，无论是通过特权还是通过专制行为。许多父母发现，一个被宠坏的孩子已经成为了家庭的老大。]

Chief, the most comprehensive of these words, can be applied to anyone who occupies the position of highest authority over a group, large or small: the editor in chief of a newspaper; the chief architect of the housing project. However, chief is more commonly used of the supervisor of some department of established government: a chief of staff; the chief inspector of weights and measures. Chief and boss are sometimes used interchangeably: I need my chief’s (or boss’s) signature on these contracts. In its original sense, a chief is the ruler of a primitive or nomadic tribe.

“酋长”这个词最全面，可以指在一个团体中担任最高权力的人，无论大小：报纸的主编；住房项目的总建筑师。常用于政府某些部门的主管：参谋长；首席度量衡员。有时可以互换使用：我需要我的主管（或老板）在这些合同上签字。 ，酋长是原始或游牧部落的统治者。

Head, like chief, is also a general term, but it is usually used of people who hold a more subordinate position than does a chief: the head of the telegraph office; the head of a boys?school; to be the head of one’s class.

Head 与 Chief 一样，也是一个通用术语，但通常用于比 Chief 地位低的人：电报局的负责人；男子学校的校长；班级。

A leader is one who is voluntarily followed because of an ability to guide and control others or because he has been chosen by a group or party to be its head. One tends to think of a leader’s having arrived at his position mainly because of his talent for influencing others and for acting as a guiding force: the leader of the German Reich; a leader in the fashion world; the leader of a labour movement.

领导者是因为有能力引导和控制他人，或者因为他被某个团体或政党选为领导者而自愿被追随的人。人们往往认为领导者之所以能达到他的地位，主要是因为他的才能。影响他人并发挥指导作用：德意志帝国的领导者；时尚界的领导者；劳工运动的领导者。

In its commonest sense a master is a person who has been given the authority to enforce obedience, but the word does not suggest the innate ability of the leader to guide and influence others. A master may be one who employs servants, is a male teacher at a school, or owns an animal, such as a dog, who can be trained to obey him. Master is also the formal title for the captain of a merchant ship. A teacher or leader in philosophy, religion, etc., who has followers or disciples is often called a master, as is Jesus by many Christians. Master is also applied to people of exceptional skill or artistic ability; a master plumber; the old masters of Renaissance painting; a master of the keyboard.

从最常见的意义上来说，主人是一个被赋予强制服从的权力的人，但这个词并不意味着领导者天生具有指导和影响他人的能力。主人可能是一个雇用仆人的人，是一位男老师。在学校里，或者拥有一只动物，比如狗，可以训练他们服从他。 大师也是对哲学、宗教等方面的老师或领导者的正式头衔。追随者或门徒通常被称为大师，正如许多基督徒所称的耶稣一样，大师也被称为水管工大师；文艺复兴时期的绘画大师。

Commander is narrower in its meaning than are the other words of this group. Originally, it meant one who commands, as a leader, chief, etc.; now it applies almost exclusively to highly placed personnel in the armed forces. In the Navy, a commander is an officer ranking next below a captain. The officer in charge of a military post is also called a commander, or commanding officer. The person holding supreme command of all the armed forces of a nation (as the Governor-General in Australia and New Zealand) is called a commander in chief, as is any high-ranking officer in charge of a fleet or a major force.

指挥官的含义比这个群体的其他词要窄，最初是指指挥者、领导者等，现在它几乎只适用于武装部队中的高级人员。指挥官是上尉以下的军官，负责军事职位的官员也称为指挥官或指挥官，负责指挥一个国家的所有武装部队（如澳大利亚的总督）。和新西兰）被称为总司令，就像任何负责舰队或主力部队的高级军官一样。

Maestro (from the Italian for master) is used of a person who is highly proficient in an artistic field; but it is now most often used of an eminent conductor, composer or performer in music. Maestro sometimes carries overtones of affectionate veneration, as in its application to the late Arturo Toscanini.

Maestro（来自意大利语，意为“大师”）用于指在艺术领域非常精通的人；但现在它最常用于音乐领域的杰出指挥家、作曲家或表演者，例如它适用于已故的阿图罗·托斯卡尼尼。

	ANTONYMS: ASSISTANT, dependant, follower, servant, subordinate, underling.


4.103 Bother
These words imply one of two situations: either one in which a person is actively annoying another or to a situation in which a person is upset by something not necessarily the actions of someone else. Some of these words can carry either the active or passive implication; other are mainly restricted to one sense or the other.

这些词暗示两种情况之一：一个人主动骚扰另一个人，或者一个人因某些不一定是其他人的行为而感到不安的情况，其中一些词可以带有主动或被动的含义。 ; 其他的主要局限于一种意义上或另一种意义上。
	
Bother, disturb and plague are often used in both active and passive senses. On the passive scale, bother usually indicates a minor complaint that may come and go: frequently bothered by a slight stiffness in his joints. Disturb is more intense, suggesting specifically, at its most extreme, mental derangement: the mentally disturbed delinquent. In milder uses, disturb points to a state of upset more thoroughgoing than that of bother: I was bothered by the lack of news at first, but now, after a month, I am really disturbed. Plague, in its passive sense, is perhaps the most intense of all these words, but suggests a specific kind of upset, one that repeatedly hammers inside the mind without pause. The person who is plagued ?by thoughts or by conditions around him ?is by implication in control neither of the things that hound or harry him nor of their recurrence within his possibly unstable mind: plagued by constant recollections of his long-dead wife; plagued by the odour in the packing plant; plagued by a continual lack of money.

打扰、打扰和瘟疫经常用于主动和被动的意义上，打扰通常表示可能会出现和消失的轻微抱怨：经常因关节轻微僵硬而烦恼，打扰更强烈，具体表明，在最极端的情况下，精神错乱：精神错乱的罪犯在较温和的用法中，扰乱指的是一种比烦扰更彻底的心烦意乱的状态：一开始我因缺乏消息而感到困扰，但现在，一个月后，我“我真的很不安”，从被动意义上来说，也许是所有这些词中最强烈的一个，但它暗示着一种特定的不安，一种不停顿地反复敲击着被思想或条件困扰的人的心灵。他周围的一切都暗示着既不控制那些困扰他的事物，也不控制它们在他可能不稳定的头脑中反复出现的情况：不断地回忆起他死去已久的妻子；受到包装厂里的气味的困扰；持续缺钱。

These same three words ?bother, disturb and plague ?give a somewhat different scale of effects in their active senses. In this case, disturb is the weakest in intensity. One person, for example, may disturb another unintentionally by actions not directed specifically to the latter: Did my whistling disturb you? Bother, here, is stronger than disturb, since an implication is present that the action may be done intentionally to disturb: Just pay the bill and I’ll stop bothering you. Plague is even stronger in the active voice than in the passive, suggesting repeated, deliberate annoyances that may have an almost demoniacal insistence: The bill collector plagued us with unrelenting phone calls, visits and threats.

同样的三个词“打扰”、“打扰”和“瘟疫”在其积极意义中给出了不同程度的影响，例如，一个人可能会因并非专门针对的行为而无意中打扰另一个人。后者：我的口哨打扰你了吗？在这里，打扰比打扰更强烈，因为存在暗示该行为可能是故意打扰的：只要付账，我就不再打扰你了。主动语态多于被动语态，暗示着重复的、故意的烦恼，可能有一种近乎恶魔般的坚持：收账人用无情的电话、拜访和威胁来困扰我们。

Trouble and worry are largely confined to the passive implication of being upset about something. [I am troubled by the doctor’s report; I’m worried that I’ll fail in the exam.] Both words are more forceful than the passive use of bother but less so than the same use of disturb. Trouble is slightly more formal than worry and suggests a definite cause for alarm; worry suggests less clear-cut reasons for uneasiness, specifically implying suspense over the outcome of something. Trouble is also more inclusive; one may be troubled without indulging in the helpless wasted motions of thought implied by worry.

麻烦和担忧很大程度上局限于对某事感到不安的被动暗示[我对医生的报告感到困扰；我担心我考试会失败。]这两个词都比被动使用的打扰更有力。但比同样使用“扰乱”的情况要少一些。“麻烦”比“担心”更正式，表示有明确的原因引起恐慌；“担心”表示不安的原因不那么明确，特别是表示对某件事的结果感到悬念。一个人可能会感到困扰，但不会沉迷于忧虑所暗示的无助的、浪费的思考动作。

In contrast, pester and harass are almost exclusively restricted to the active sense of someone annoying another person. [The platoon sergeant constantly harassed his men in ingeniously excruciating ways; Stop pestering me!] Both words are more forceful than the active use of disturb and even of bother. Pester is like the active use of plague in suggesting repeated and deliberate annoyances that interrupt someone else, but remains restricted mainly to trivial matters. Harass is considerably stronger, even carrying the possibility of physical punishment or worse: guerillas nightly harassing the border villages. Harass may even be stronger than plague in this case, since the latter stops short of any implication of physical violence.

相比之下，“pester”和“harass”几乎完全局限于某人骚扰另一个人的主动含义[排长不断地以巧妙而令人难以忍受的方式骚扰他的部下；别再缠着我了！]这两个词都比主动使用“干扰”和“干扰”更有力。即使是骚扰，也类似于积极使用瘟疫来暗示重复和故意打扰别人，但骚扰的程度要大得多，甚至可能带来体罚或更糟的情况：游击队每晚骚扰别人。在这种情况下，骚扰甚至可能比瘟疫更严重，因为没有任何人身暴力的影响。

SEE: ANGER, ENRAGE, UPSET.
	ANTONYMS: comfort, console, placate, solace.


4.104 Bounce
All these words describe ways in which the direction of a moving object can be radically changed. Bounce, the most general term, ban  be applied to virtually any missile that rebounds, such as a ball, stone, coin apple, etc. [He didn’t see me toss him the book; it bounced off his chest and fell to the floor.] But bounce commonly emphasizes resiliency. [The basketball bounced high in the air; My little girl loves to bounce up and down on her bed.]	
	
所有这些词都描述了可以从根本上改变移动物体方向的方式“反弹”，这是最通用的术语，几乎可以应用于任何反弹的导弹，例如球、石头、金苹果等。[他没有。我没看到我把书扔给他；它从他的胸口弹起，掉到了地板上。]但是弹跳通常强调弹性[篮球在空中弹得很高；我的小女孩喜欢在床上弹来弹去。 .]

Cannon is a curious word, because the noun refers to a highly skilful and carefully controlled billiards shot, whereas the verb often implies lack of control and recklessness. In billiards, a cannon is a shot in which the cue ball strikes against two other balls in succession. As a verb, cannon means to hit and rebound, often in a context that implies that the rebound is uncontrolled and damaging. [The car cannoned off the telephone pole and hurtled into a parked mail van.]

Cannon 是一个奇怪的词，因为这个名词指的是一种高度熟练且精心控制的台球击球，而动词则通常意味着缺乏控制和鲁莽。在台球中，cannon 是指母球撞击另外两个球的击球。作为动词，“大炮”的意思是“撞击和反弹”，通常在暗示反弹不受控制且具有破坏性的情况下[汽车从电线杆上轰出，冲进一辆停着的邮车。]

Deflect means to turn aside or cause something to swerve from its course. Ricochet means to glance from a surface in the fashion of a stone thrown over the surface of water, making a series of skips or bounds. Thus ricochet in practice means to bounce away fast, with little loss of speed, whereas deflect stresses the change in direction of a moving object. Compare these two examples. [The bullet ricocheted off the pavement and shattered the window glass; The arrow, deflected by strong winds, missed its target completely.] In some contexts ricochet and cannon are interchangeable, but cannon emphasizes collision and the force of the rebound whereas ricochet emphasizes the speed of the deflection. Bounce can substituted in most contexts for cannon and ricochet, but not for deflect; deflect differs essentially from the other words in not involving the actions of bounding away or collision. It means what the others only imply: a change in the direction of movement of an object.

偏转的意思是转向一边或导致某物偏离其路线。 弹跳的意思是像扔到水面上的石头一样从表面上看，产生一系列的跳跃或跳跃，因此弹跳实际上意味着弹开。速度快，速度损失很小，而偏转则强调移动物体方向的变化[子弹从人行道上弹开，打碎了窗户玻璃；箭头被强风偏转，完全偏离了目标。 .] 在某些情况下，弹跳和大炮可以互换，但大炮强调碰撞和反弹力，而弹跳则强调偏转速度，在大多数情况下可以替代大炮和弹跳，但与偏转没有本质上的不同；换句话说，不涉及弹跳或碰撞的动作，这意味着其他词仅暗示：物体运动方向的改变。


4.105 Boundary
These words denote a line that marks the outermost part of an area, or a division between areas. Boundary is used chiefly of territory, and suggests a definite demarcation, such as a line or mark that can be precisely located on a map. Bounds are less definite, and may be used figuratively of behaviour: His impudence exceeds all bounds. In military usage out of bounds serves to notify military personnel not to enter the building or area so stigmatized. This use is extended to any area forbidden to certain persons: The girl’s recreation area in the school is out of bounds to boys. The colloquial expression out of bounds, derived from its use in various sports, is commonly used with the meaning of unfair, improper or indecent: Holding hands was out of bounds, and as for kissing ?that was unthinkable.

这些词表示标记区域最外部的线，或区域之间的分界线，主要用于领土，并表示明确的分界线，例如可以在地图上精确定位的线或标记。不太明确，可以比喻性地使用：他的无礼超出了所有界限。在军事用途中，out ofbounds 是为了通知军事人员不要进入受到污名化的建筑物或区域。这种用法扩展到任何禁止某些人进入的区域：学校里的女生休闲区对男生来说是禁区 这个口语表达“out ofbound”源自其在各种体育运动中的使用，通常具有不公平、不正当或不雅的含义：牵手是禁区，并且至于接吻？那是不可想象的。

Whereas boundary points to an outermost limit, border emphasizes the division between two areas: the border between the U.S.S.R. and Finland. [He crossed the border into Belgium; By international agreement the boundary of each nation fronting a body of water extends exactly three miles from the coastline.] Border often suggests a territorial feature, such as a river or mountain range, and hence is not as precise as boundary. Boundaries may be changed by treaties, i.e. on paper; borders may change by the changing course of a river or by military action.

除了边界指向最外面的界限外，边界强调两个区域之间的划分：苏联和芬兰之间的边界[他越过边界进入比利时；根据国际协议，每个国家面向水域的边界正好延伸三英里。 ] 边界通常表示领土特征，例如河流或山脉，因此边界不像条约那样精确，即在纸面上，边界可能会因河流或山脉的走向而改变。通过军事行动。

Limit is the most general term of this group, and can be applied to any outermost extent, range, demarcation, etc. as here considered the term is usually plural: to pass beyond the city limits. Frontier may refer to the part of a nation’s territory lying along the border of another country; it thus describes the border region of a country from an interior perspective. Frontier also means the part of a settled region lying along the border of an unsettled region; the frontier towns of the American Wild West. Frontier is often used in extended senses; beyond the frontier of knowledge; at the frontier of space exploration.

限制是该组中最通用的术语，可以应用于任何最外层的范围、范围、分界等，因为这里认为该术语通常是复数的：超越城市边界可以指一个国家的一部分。位于另一个国家边境的领土；因此，它从内部角度描述了一个国家的边境地区，也意味着位于美国狂野西部边境城镇的定居地区的一部分。前沿通常用于扩展意义；超越知识的前沿；空间探索的前沿。

Confines, like bounds, defines the extent of an area without reference to what lies beyond, but confines is less consistently restricted to the description of geographical limits: He was not permitted to pass beyond the confines of his room. Confines, like bounds, is commonly used figuratively: His genius soared beyond the narrow confines of his education; beyond all bounds of decency or common sense.

界限，就像界限一样，定义了一个区域的范围，而不涉及超出的范围，但界限不太一致地局限于地理限制的描述：他不被允许超出他房间的界限。 界限，就像界限一样，是不允许的。通常用来比喻：他的天才超越了他所受教育的狭隘范围；超越了一切正派或常识的界限。

SEE: CIRCUMSCRIBE, EDGE, PERIMETER.


4.106 Brand
These words can all be used to describe commercial names, commodities, and services, and are in this sense related; but they are not synonyms, and there are important distinctions of fact to be made between them. Brand is generally understood to mean a definite, usually well-known and advertised type of commodity: the Lipton brand of tea; a popular brand of cigarettes. By extension, brand name identifies a whole group of products made or sold by the same enterprise: Westinghouse is the brand name of a line of electrical appliances.

这些词都可以用来描述商业名称、商品和服务，并且在这个意义上是相关的；但它们不是同义词，并且它们之间存在重要的区别。 ，通常是知名且广告宣传的商品类型：立顿品牌的茶；推而广之，品牌名称标识同一企业生产或销售的整个产品组：西屋电气是一个系列的品牌名称。的电器。

Trademark (sometimes hyphenated as a trade-mark) comes closet to having a definite legal status, especially when formally registered with the appropriate government agency. Legally, a trademark is a word, symbol, device or any combination thereof adopted and used by a manufacturer or merchant to identify his goods and distinguish them from those manufactured and sold by others. Of the thousands in active use, most take the form of words, as Kodak, Vaseline, Technicolor, Coca-Cola, Dacron, etc. it will be noted that such words are spelt with an initial capital letter, a practice strongly recommended by their owners as a means of emphasizing exclusive rights to the good will and equity inherent in their commercial use.
	
商标（有时用连字符作为商标）几乎具有明确的法律地位，特别是在适当的政府机构正式注册后。 从法律上讲，商标是制造商采用和使用的文字、符号、图案或其任意组合。或商人识别他的商品并将其与其他人制造和销售的商品区分开来，大多数采用文字形式，如柯达、凡士林、特艺、可口可乐、涤纶等。这些单词的首字母大写，这是其所有者强烈推荐的做法，作为强调商业使用中固有的善意和公平的专有权利的一种手段。

Trade name, though used as a variant of trademark, is legally synonymous with the commercial name under which a firm, enterprise, corporation, association, etc. conducts its business. [3M Company is the trade name of a manufacturer of industrial products, many of which carry trademarks.]

商号虽然用作商标的变体，但在法律上是公司、企业、公司、协会等开展业务的商业名称的同义词[3M 公司是工业产品制造商的商号。其中带有商标。]

A logotype is any single piece of type containing several letters, a word or words. In advertising, logotype applies specifically to a particular design or style used to represent the name of a company or a trade mark so as to make it more readily identifiable and emphasizes its protected status in the public mind. Thus there are logotypes ?or logos, as they are called for short ?for may well-known trademarks.

标识是包含多个字母、一个或多个单词的任何单个字体，在广告中，标识专门适用于代表公司名称或商标的特定设计或风格，以便更容易识别和使用。强调其在公众心目中的受保护地位，因此出现了标识（或徽标），因为它们是驰名商标的缩写。

A colophon was formerly an inscription placed at the end of a books, showing the title, the printer’s name, date and other information, such as the style and size of type used. Now the word is more commonly used to refer to a design or emblem adopted by a publisher to represent a particular line of books or the publishing house as a whole; the colophon is usually printed on the title page of books.

版权页以前是放置在书籍末尾的铭文，显示标题、印刷商名称、日期和其他信息，例如所用字体的样式和大小。现在，该词更常用于指设计或设计。出版商采用的标志，代表特定系列的书籍或整个出版社；版权页通常印在书籍的扉页上。


4.107 Brandish
These words are synonyms when they mean to move something rapidly back and forth or in circles. Brandish means to wave or shake a weapon, especially in public, so as to threaten or intimidate someone: The drunk at the bar suddenly brandished a gun, and everybody scrambled for cover. Flourish implies a display of self-confidence, triumph or merely high-spirits: The victorious army flourished a captured flag.

这些词是同义词，意思是快速地来回移动某物或绕圈移动。 Brandish 的意思是挥舞或摇动武器，尤其是在公共场合，以威胁或恐吓某人：酒吧里的醉汉突然挥舞着枪，然后。每个人都争先恐后地寻找掩护，这意味着自信、胜利或仅仅是兴高采烈的表现：胜利的军队挥舞着缴获的旗帜。

Swing, in this sense, means to move rhythmically to and fro or backwards and forwards, like the pendulum of a clock or the clapper of a bell. It may imply a wide, sweeping motion, even rotation: to swing an axe; Huckleberry Finn recommended swinging a dead cat over one’s head to cure warts. Wield emphasizes the command one has over the sue of a weapon or instrument: to wield a hammer and chisel; to wield forceps with consummate skill. Sometimes wield approaches brandish in meaning: He turned to towards me and suddenly wielded a short, ugly knife.

从这个意义上说，“摇摆”意味着有节奏地前后或前后移动，就像钟摆或钟声一样。它可能意味着广泛的、扫过的动作，甚至旋转：挥舞斧头；建议用一只死猫在头上挥舞来治疗疣，强调一个人对武器或工具的指挥：挥舞锤子和凿子；有时挥舞的意思是挥舞。突然向我挥舞着一把又短又丑的刀。

	ANTONYMS: arrest, hang, suspend.
	
	
4.108 Brashness
These words describe shameless, bold or arrogantly brusque behaviour. Brashness indicates a decisive, insistently aggressive or come-what-may attitude. When the word is approving, it expresses wonder or admiration for someone’s audacity and zest; more commonly, it is used to criticize a rash lack of judgement or a lack of consideration for others: the brashness of such a small country in successfully defending itself against its enemies; a foolhardy brashness that often tempted him to tackle situations he knew nothing about; the brashness with which he pushed his way to the top of the heap, injuring the feelings of everyone else in the office. The word can also point to a garish vulgarity of taste: The brashness of his sports clothes almost made my eyeballs ache. Sauciness suggests, instead, an imperious, insouciant and haughty manner, often exhibited in an inferior or in someone replying sharply or out of turn: the sauciness of that impertinent little salesgirl; the indignant sauciness with which he refused to take his nap. Often, the word can be used humorously or affectionately to describe the spirited display of someone who is weak or powerless: the roguish sauciness of a small kitten: the boy’s sauciness in grandly declining to play house with his older sister.
	
这些词描述了无耻、大胆或傲慢的行为，表示一种果断、坚持侵略或不择手段的态度。批评鲁莽地缺乏判断力或缺乏对他人的考虑：这样一个小国在抵御敌人时的鲁莽鲁莽常常诱使他去处理他一无所知的情况；他一路走上巅峰，伤害了办公室里其他人的感情，这个词也可以暗示一种花哨粗俗的品味：他的运动服的傲慢几乎让我的眼球感到疼痛，相反，它暗示着一种专横。 ，漫不经心和傲慢的态度，经常表现出低人一等或尖锐或不合时宜的回答：那个无礼的小女售货员的无礼；他拒绝午睡时的愤怒无礼通常，这个词可以用幽默或幽默的方式使用。亲切地形容弱者或无能为力的人的活泼表现：小猫的顽皮俏皮；男孩堂而皇之地拒绝和姐姐一起玩过家家的俏皮。

The remaining words are all extremely informal words for the idea of brazen insolence and self-seeking. Of these, however, only nerve can function with either positive or negative force. When approving, the word points to cool self-possession and courage in acting against odds: It took nerve for him to stand up for his rights in an atmosphere thick with recrimination and threats of reprisal. In disapproval, nerve suggests a shameless disregard for good taste or manners: Imagine the nerve of him, asking her to stay with him for the night! Brass, hide and cheek indicate an insistent and insolent self-assurance. Brass is the most disapproving of the three, suggesting a coarse or ingrained lack of sensitivity to the feelings of others: He had the brass to tell me I had no right to correct him. Hide is less strong but still has a connotation of deliberately insensitive behaviour: the hide of him, arriving 40 minutes late. Cheek is milder in suggesting a smug self-regard that prompts uncritical, brazen or tasteless behaviour: the cheek to ask for a rise after a week in his new job. Like sauciness, the word can be used humorously or affectionately for a cute forwardness in one’s inferiors: the cheek of the boy in asking for another helping of dessert. Gall is the most severely disapproving of all these words, suggesting shameless acts of unwarranted discourtesy: the gall to invite himself to tea. But the word is very general, applying to any act one dislikes.

其余的词都是非常非正式的词，表示厚颜无耻和自私自利，但是，只有神经才能在赞同时发挥积极或消极的力量。在反对的情况下采取行动：他需要勇气在充满相互指责和报复威胁的气氛中维护自己的权利，在不赞成的情况下，勇气意味着对良好品味或礼仪的无耻漠视：想象一下他要求她这样做的勇气。和他一起过夜！黄铜，隐藏和脸颊表明了一种坚持和傲慢的自信。黄铜是三者中最不赞成的，表明对他人的感受粗鲁或根深蒂固的缺乏敏感性：他有黄铜要告诉。对我来说，我没有权利纠正他。隐藏的行为不那么强烈，但仍然有严重麻木不仁的含义：他迟到了 40 分钟，它更温和地暗示了一种自以为是的自尊，导致不批判、厚颜无耻或无品位。行为：新工作一周后厚颜无耻地要求加薪，就像“傲慢”一样，这个词可以幽默地或亲切地用来形容下属的可爱的率性：男孩厚颜无耻地要求再吃一份甜点。对所有这些词最严厉的反对是，暗示无礼无礼的无耻行为：无礼地请自己喝茶，但这个词非常笼统，适用于任何人不喜欢的行为。

SEE: CONCEITED, EFFR0NTERY, OVERBEARING.
	ANTONYMS: civility, meekness, politeness, self-effacement.
	

4.109 Brave
These words indicate a readiness to face danger, difficulty or even death when called upon by circumstances to do so. Brave is the most general word. It indicates the showing of one’s mettle under stress, implying self-possession and resolution. Courageous, like brave, may focus on response to a situation, but it often implies firmness arising from strong moral convictions. Both words imply a willingness to proceed with the necessary in spite of external deterrents or internal misgivings. A brave or courageous soldier carries out a dangerous mission, not without fear, but without letting fear prevent him from doing his duty.
	
这些词表示在情况需要时愿意面对危险、困难甚至死亡。勇敢是最普遍的词，它表示一个人在压力下表现出的勇气，就像勇敢一样。 ，可能侧重于对情况的反应，但它通常意味着坚定的道德信念，这两个词都意味着尽管有外部威慑或内部疑虑，仍愿意采取必要的行动，勇敢或勇敢的士兵执行危险的任务。并非没有恐惧，但不要让恐惧阻止他履行职责。

Dauntless and undaunted indicate bravery under exceptionally trying circumstances. Both imply a refusal to be disheartened, intimidated or otherwise discouraged from going on. [Scientists pursue their experiments with dauntless determination, despite repeated failures and disappointments; Stalemated negotiators must resume their talks each day with undaunted optimism.] Fearless and intrepid imply a resolute freedom from fear or a cool, unshakable determination. [A fearless, crusading newspaper exposes corruption in high places without being deterred by the danger of reprisal; The intrepid explorers hacked their way through the jungle in spite of the constant danger of native attack.]

无畏和无畏都表示在异常艰难的情况下的勇敢。 两者都意味着拒绝灰心丧气、恐吓或因其他原因而灰心丧气地继续下去。无所畏惧的乐观主义意味着坚决摆脱恐惧或冷静、不可动摇的决心[一份无所畏惧的十字军报纸揭露了高层的腐败行为，而没有被报复的危险所吓倒；勇敢的探险家在丛林中开辟了一条道路。尽管存在持续的本地攻击危险。]

Valiant and valorous are applied to persons and actions that exhibit the kind of courage and fortitude associated with knighthood. Valiant may suggest bravery shown in a worthy cause, against impossible odds, or with commendable consequences. Valorous is usually applied to the spirit or deeds of the valiant. A valiant fireman may save persons trapped in a burning building by a valorous disregard of his own safety.

Valiant 和 valorous 指表现出与骑士精神相关的勇气和毅力的人和行为，Valiant 可能表示在一项有价值的事业中表现出的勇敢，克服不可能的困难，或取得值得赞扬的后果。勇敢的消防员可以不顾自身安危，勇敢地拯救被困在燃烧建筑物中的人们。

Heroic and gallant outstanding bravery coupled with nobility of motive or selfless dedication. Heroic stresses exceptional courage, fortitude or enterprise, especially in time of war or danger. It implies a willingness to risk or sacrifice one’s life to save another or others. Gallant implies inner nobility that is manifested in chivalrous action. [The storming of Gallipoli was a heroic action of gallant men.]

英雄和英勇 杰出的勇敢加上高尚的动机或无私的奉献精神，英雄强调非凡的勇气、毅力或进取心，特别是在战争或危险时期，它意味着愿意冒着生命危险或牺牲自己的生命来拯救他人或他人。 [攻克加里波利是勇敢者的英雄行为。]

Plucky is a somewhat informal word, usually applied to contenders who persist against unfavourable odds. A plucky prize-fighter does his best to hold his own against a heavier, more skilful opponent. Bold indicates an actively brave nature or a confident audacity. The bold man is daring and is undeterred by fear of consequences: the R.A.F.’s bold bombing of the Ruhr dams in 1943 spread destruction across Germany’s industrial heartland.

勇敢是一个非正式的词，通常用于指在不利的情况下坚持不懈的竞争者，勇敢的职业拳击手尽最大努力对抗更重、更有技巧的对手。人类是勇敢的，不会因担心后果而被吓倒：1943 年英国皇家空军对鲁尔大坝的大胆轰炸给德国工业中心地带带来了破坏。

SEE: BOLD, DARING, RECKLESS.
	ANTONYMS: AFRAID, COWARDLY, daunted, intimidated, TIMID.
	

4.110 Break
These words refer to the forcible destruction, breaching or injury of something. Break is the most general word. It most often suggests the separation of a rigid body into pieces, implying either partial or total destruction of a whole: breaking the firewood in two for easier burning; breaking a vase by accident. Break may also indicate a temporary injury, as to a bone: breaking a leg in a fall. And it may involve getting free from some restraint or enclosure: to break out of goal; buds breaking open. Burst is close to break in this latter sense but involves much greater violence. It is highly specific word, suggesting a forceful breaking open that is due to internal pressure: squeezing a pimple until it bursts open; a dam so weakened by floods that it finally burst; blowing up a balloon until it bursts.

这些词指的是对某物的强行破坏、破坏或伤害，它最常表示将刚性体分成碎片，暗示整体的部分或全部破坏：将木柴劈成两半。更容易燃烧；意外打破花瓶也可能表示暂时受伤：跌倒时摔断腿；并且可能涉及摆脱某些限制或围栏：花蕾破开；破裂在后一种意义上接近破裂，但涉及更大的暴力，这是一个非常具体的词，表明由于内部压力而产生的强力破裂：挤压一个疙瘩，直到它破裂；一座被洪水削弱的水坝，最终破裂。爆裂；吹气球直到爆裂。

Crack usually means to break without separation of parts. It suggests the breaking out across a surface of slit-like openings or hairline ruptures, either because of wear, age or pressure: a window that he cracked by leaning against it; a cracked cup; linoleum that had faded and cracked. In other uses, crack may mean to break apart or break into pieces: Cracking open the walnut without breaking the kernel. Fracture can suggest a deeper, more thorough, but also more localized breaking than crack: fracturing the bone in two places; boulders fractured by continual freezing and thawing; old habit patterns fractured by changing technology.

裂纹通常意味着由于磨损、老化或压力而在表面上出现裂缝状开口或发丝状破裂：靠在破裂的杯子上而破裂的窗户；在其他用途​​中，裂纹可能意味着裂开或碎成碎片：在不破坏核桃仁的情况下，裂纹可以表示比裂纹更深、更彻底、但也更局部的破裂：使核桃破裂。骨头在两处；巨石因不断的冻结和融化而断裂；旧的习惯模式因技术的变化而断裂。

Shatter and shiver most often suggest a total breaking up of a thin surface. Shatter is the more general of the two, implying the breaking of such a surface into sharp pieces or jagged fragments: heavy enough to shatter the melting ice; a well-aimed stone that shattered the already cracked window. The word can, however, refer to the breaking of any brittle object, in which case, it suggests reduction to many fairly small pieces: a marble statue that had been completely shattered in the earthquake. Shiver, by contrast, is more closely restricted to glass or glass-like surfaces, suggesting a reduction into long, narrow shards or slivers: shivering the mirror. The word might now seem outdated except as a noun.

破碎和颤抖通常表示薄表面的完全破裂。破碎是两者中较为普遍的一种，意味着将这样的表面破碎成锋利的碎片或锯齿状的碎片：重量足以粉碎融化的冰；然而，这个词可以指任何易碎物体的破碎，在这种情况下，它意味着破碎成许多相当小的碎片：在地震中完全破碎的大理石雕像，相比之下，“颤抖的镜子”更严格地局限于玻璃或类似玻璃的表面，表明它被简化为又长又窄的碎片或条子：“颤抖的镜子”除了作为名词之外，现在似乎已经过时了。

Crush and smash suggest forceful action taken to destroy or break something. Crush points to the effect of great external pressure: it suggests squeezing something out of shape: crushing the empty cigarette packed in one hand; eggs that had been crushed by tinned goods placed on top of them in the carton. Smash describes the kind of complete deformation resulting from a heavy, noisy blow. This word suggests the shattering of something brittle either by throwing it or by throwing something against it: smashing the window with his bare fist: He smashed the bottle to smithereens against the rocks.

“crush”和“smash”表示为破坏或破坏某物而采取的强力行动“Crush”指的是外部巨大压力的作用：它表示将某物挤压变形：用一只手压碎装在罐头物品上的空香烟； “粉碎”描述了因重击而产生的完全变形，这个词暗示着通过扔东西或用东西撞碎易碎的东西：用拳头砸碎窗户：他。把瓶子撞在岩石上，摔成了碎片。

SEE: CRACK, DESTROY, EXPLODE.
	ANTONYMS: CONNECT REPAIR, weld.
	
	
4.111 Bright
All these words refer most specifically to the intense, steady light emitted from a source, rather than to wavering or reflected light. Bright is the most general of these, stressing chiefly the intensity of the light: the bright stars. It is more useful than the other words as a comparative: the brighter of the two neon signs. In its very generality, bright permits reference to wavering or reflected light, but only to emphasize intensity: a bright, cheerful fire; sun-bright ripples. Brilliant lends itself to the same uses as bright, but suggests even greater intensity: brilliant head-lights. Brilliant can have a lyrical quality absent in the more matter-of-fact bright, and consequently it can imply excellence or beauty: the brilliant, cloudless day.

所有这些词最具体地指的是从光源发出的强烈、稳定的光，而不是波动或反射的光。“明亮”是其中最笼统的，主要强调光的强度：“明亮的星星”比“明亮的星星”更有用。另一个词作为比较：两个霓虹灯标志中较亮的一个，一般来说，“明亮”可以指波动或反射的光，但只是为了强调强度：明亮、欢快的火焰适合于阳光般明亮的涟漪。与“明亮”的用法相同，但暗示更大的强度：“辉煌”可以具有更实际的“明亮”所没有的抒情品质，因此它可以暗示卓越或美丽：灿烂、万里无云的日子。

Incandescent suggests light created specifically by combustion, and it may or may not carry overtones of emitted warmth as well as light. Incandescent may simply refer technically to a white-hot light: an incandescent lamp. In other uses it suggests fierceness or intense whiteness rather than the excellence or beauty of brilliant: the incandescent glare of the street lights.

白炽灯表示专门由燃烧产生的光，它可能会或可能不会带有发出的温暖和光的色彩，从技术上讲，白炽灯可能只是指白炽灯：在其他用途​​中，它表示强烈或强烈的白色。比辉煌的卓越或美丽更重要：路灯的白炽眩光。

Resplendent is in every way an intensification of brilliant; though more formal, it is even more lyrical, stressing vivid brightness and dazzling splendour: the resplendent sun; a sky resplendent with stars. Resplendent can refer to sources of reflected light as well, but with the same lyrical force and implication of lustre, bedecked with diamonds and resplendent in her jewelled gown.

从各方面来说，灿烂都是辉煌的强化；虽然更正式，但更抒情，强调生动的亮度和令人眼花缭乱的辉煌：辉煌的太阳；灿烂的星星也可以指反射光的来源。同样的抒情力量和光泽的含义，镶满了钻石，在她的珠宝礼服上熠熠生辉。

Effulgent is like resplendent in lyricism and formality except that it is more precisely restricted to sources of light. Also, its extreme formality may make its use seem inflated or pretentious: effulgent rays streaming through the thunderhead.

Effulgent在抒情性和形式上就像辉煌一样，只不过它更精确地局限于光源。此外，它的极端形式可能使它的使用看起来夸大或自命不凡：明亮的光线流过雷雨云。

While far less formal than resplendent or effulgent, shining as an adjective has been so overworked when used with lyrical intent that it may now strike one as a cliché in most contexts: a knight in shining armour. Shining may escape this liability when it is merely descriptive: the shining beacon far out at sea. Used in such a way, it contrasts with all the foregoing words by describing light that need not necessarily be intense. Glowing and radiant, similarly, do not emphasize intensity. Glowing suggests a slow burning or the last stage of burning; it implies warmth as well, but faintness of both light and warmth may be the point of its use: the glowing remains of a fire. Radiant suggests the emission of light in all directions; it carries a unique connotation of mild, gentle warmth: a radiant spring day, so unlike those of incandescent summer. Beaming refers specifically to light sent out in long arms, either stationary or sweeping: the beaming searchlight.

虽然“闪亮”远没有“辉煌”或“辉煌”那么正式，但当用于抒情意图时，“闪亮”这个形容词已经被过度使用，以至于在大多数情况下它可能会让人觉得是陈词滥调：穿着闪亮盔甲的骑士可能会逃脱这种责任，而它仅仅是这样。描述性：远方的闪亮灯塔以这种方式使用，与前面所有的词形成鲜明对比，它描述不一定是强烈的光，同样，发光并不强调强度。燃烧的最后阶段；它也暗示着温暖，但光的微弱和温暖可能是它的用途：发光的余烬暗示着向四面八方发射光；温和、温柔的温暖：与白炽夏日不同的是，光芒四射的春日特指长臂发出的光，无论是静止的还是扫射的：光束探照灯。

All these words can refer figuratively to qualities of personality, intelligence or passion. Indeed, their metaphorical use has been extensive in describing all that is good or desirable in human nature ?perhaps a comment on the high value man has continued to place on light. In brief, bright refers to intelligence, but more as potential than as accomplishment: a bright student. Brilliant goes beyond bright to indicate great intellect or talent. It may also refer to a highly admired accomplishment or illustrious achievement: a brilliant novel. Resplendent may suggest the blaze and brilliance of triumph or majesty: soldiers resplendent in victory. Effulgent may describe something that seems to radiate outwards like light: her effulgent loveliness. Glowing suggests their satisfaction ?or a being possessed by calmer, gentler feelings: eyes glowing with desire; a face radiant with tenderness. Beaming suggests pleasure or self-satisfaction, while shining in most of its figurative uses is decidedly trite.

所有这些词都可以象征性地指代人格、智慧或激情的品质。事实上，它们的隐喻用途广泛地描述了人性中所有美好或令人向往的事物——也许对人类高价值的评论仍然存在于光之上。简而言之，“聪明”指的是智力，但更多的是指潜力而不是成就：“聪明的学生”不仅指聪明才智或才华横溢，还可以指令人高度赞赏的成就或杰出的成就：辉煌的小说。表示胜利或威严的火焰和光辉：胜利中辉煌的士兵可能会描述一些似乎像光一样向外辐射的东西：她的光辉灿烂表示他们的满足——或者是一种被更平静、更温和的情感所占据的感觉：眼睛里闪烁着渴望。 ; 容光焕发的面孔暗示着快乐或自我满足，而闪耀在其大多数比喻用法中显然是陈词滥调。

SEE: LUMINOUS, SPARKLING.
	ANTONYMS: dim, dull, GLOOMY, OBSCURE, opaque.
	
	
4.112 Brusque
All these words point to a shortness or discourtesy of manner in a person’s treatment of others. Brusque derives from an Italian word meaning rude. It is applied to a noticeably short, brisk or terse manner that may or may not be rude, depending on intent and circumstance. [A no-nonsense woman, the governess gave her employer a brusque handshake; Being in a hurry, he made an unintentionally brusque reply.] At worst, brusque may imply incivility, ungracious sharpness or undue severity: a brusque dismissal. Bluff, by contrast, is not at all negative in tone but implies a hearty frankness ?an openness that may lack finesse but does not intend discourtesy. Bluff is used almost exclusively to describe men. The bluff man talks and laughs loudly and freely, says and does whatever he pleases with fearless good nature, and with no thought of annoying or giving pain to others: A bluff, beefy man, he didn’t mince his words, but there was a twinkle in his eye. Blunt is fairly close to bluff at one extreme, though it can imply only a well-meaning directness. Unlike bluff, however, blunt more often suggests a flat-footed forthrightness that verges on discourtesy. It may describe a manner of speech as well as a person. [Shall I lie politely to you, or shall I be blunt? Be as blunt as you like ?I won’t mind your rudeness if you tell me the truth.] At the other extreme, blunt may indicate a tactless frankness that is inconsiderate or needlessly cruel. The blunt man may say things which he is perfectly aware are disagreeable, either from a defiant indifference to others?feelings or from the pleasure of tormenting. Short has a connotation of quickness and directness, with a hint of anger and perhaps rudeness: I was very short with him for asking such a foolish question.

所有这些词都表示一个人对待他人的粗鲁或无礼行为，Brusque 源自意大利语，意思是粗鲁，它适用于明显简短、轻快或简洁的方式，可能是粗鲁的，也可能不是粗鲁的。 [一个严肃的女人，家庭女教师粗鲁地与她的雇主握手；由于匆忙，他无意中粗鲁地回答了。] 在最坏的情况下，粗鲁可能意味着不礼貌、不礼貌的尖锐或过度严厉：粗鲁的解雇。相比之下，“虚张声势”的语气一点也不消极，而是暗示一种真诚的坦诚——一种可能缺乏技巧但无意无礼的开放性。“虚张声势”几乎专门用来形容男人大声而自由地说话和笑。他怀着无所畏惧的善良本性做任何他想做的事，没有想到会惹恼或给别人带来痛苦：他是一个直言不讳、强健的人，说话毫不拐弯抹角，但他的眼睛里闪烁着相当接近的光芒。虚张声势在一个极端，虽然它只能意味着善意的直接，然而，与虚张声势不同，直率更经常意味着一种近乎无礼的直率。我有礼貌地对你撒谎，还是应该直言不讳？如果你告诉我真相，我不会介意你的粗鲁。] 在另一个极端，直言不讳可能表示不体贴或不必要的坦率。直率的人可能会说一些他完全意识到的令人不快的话，要么是出于对他人感情的挑衅冷漠，要么是出于折磨的乐趣。我对他提出这样一个愚蠢的问题感到很生气。

Abrupt and curt both suggest an uncooperative terseness, especially in reply to a question or appeal for help. His laconic answers to my repeated requests for directions were both unfriendly and abrupt.

唐突和生硬都表明了一种不合作的简洁，尤其是在回答问题或寻求帮助时，他对我反复询问的简洁回答既不友好又唐突。

Abrupt may also imply a disconcerting directness: an abrupt refusal. Curt is stronger than abrupt, implying hardness or coldness of manner as well as a willful intent to be unpleasant: a curt rejoinder. [I can understand being a little abrupt if one is really busy, but she’s always curt even when she’s just wasting her time.]

突然的拒绝也可能意味着令人不安的直接：突然的拒绝比突然的拒绝更强烈，暗示着态度的强硬或冷漠以及故意令人不愉快：简短的反驳[如果一个人真的很突然，我可以理解。很忙，但即使她只是在浪费时间，她也总是很简短。]

Gruff and surly suggest bad-tempered or rude behaviour; but they need not imply either straightforwardness, as in bluff and blunt, or undue brevity of response, as in abrupt and curt. Of the two words, gruff is more appropriately applied to a man and is most applicable to disposition. It describes one who is brusque, rough and crusty in manner or hoarse and guttural in speech. [He’ll grumble for minutes at a time when he’s gruff and grouchy, but don’t expect a straight answer from him then.] Surly suggests extreme discourtesy and may be applied to either sex. It implies not so much a sour frame of mind as an abiding attitude of hostility to people ?a crabbed, churlish disposition evident in both speech and manner: a surly, insubordinate servant. [Give me the gruffest salesman in the world and I won’t complain ?just so long as I don’t have to put up with that surly woman in the lingerie department. I’ll even take the blunt remarks about my figure from the woman in the dress department or the curt answers of the credit manager when I ask to pay by cheque. Believe me, a surly salesgirl is far worse.]

gruff 和 surly 表示脾气暴躁或粗鲁的行为；但它们不一定意味着直率（如虚张声势和直率），也不一定意味着反应过于简短（如唐突和生硬），在这两个词中，gruff 更适合用于男人。它最适用于性格粗暴、粗鲁、脾气暴躁或说话声音嘶哑、喉咙发哑的人[当他粗暴、脾气暴躁时，他会抱怨几分钟，但不要指望得到直接的回答。 ] 粗暴的意思是极端的无礼，可以适用于任何性别。与其说它意味着一种阴郁的心态，不如说是一种对人持久的敌意态度——一种在言语和举止上都明显表现出来的乖戾、粗暴的性格：一种粗暴的态度。 ，不听话的仆人。 [给我一个世界上最粗鲁的推销员，我不会抱怨？只要我不必忍受内衣部门那个脾气暴躁的女人，我什至会接受关于她的直言不讳的言论。服装部那位女士的身材或者当我要求用支票付款时信贷经理的简短回答相信我，一个脾气暴躁的女售货员的情况要糟糕得多。]

SEE: CANDID, TERSE.
	ANTONYMS: diplomatic, gracious, mannerly, POLITE, tactful, unctuous, URBANE.

	
4.113 Bug
These words relate to a large and varied division of invertebrate animals. Bug and wog are names loosely applied to any very small creeping, crawling, jumping or flying creature that is generally thought of as a nuisance. Wog is the more informal and is even applied to the completely unrelated bacteria and viruses that cause disease, especially a cold which is "going around": Sorry I can’t go ?I’ve got the wog. Bug is the least specific word in the group, but arthropod is the inclusive, zoological term. Arthropods have no backbone; they are characterized by jointed legs or appendages, segmented body parts and usually, hard outer coverings. The true bugs belong to a special order of arthropods whose members have biting or sucking mouth parts, such as bedbugs, water bugs and plant bugs. Beetles also have biting mouth parts and have hard, horny fore wings that cover and protect their hind wings. Bugs and beetles form part of the largest class of arthropods, the insects. There are close to a million kinds of insects, all having bodies divided into three sections, each of which carries a pair of legs, making six legs in all. This characteristic distinguishes insects from spiders, which have eight legs and which, with scorpions, mites and ticks, are placed in another separate class of arthropods, the arachnids. The class of crustaceans includes shrimps, crabs, lobsters, barnacles and crayfish, living mostly in or near water. Crustaceans are characterized by tough outer shells that are shed by moulting as they grow larger.

这些词与大量不同的无脊椎动物有关，Bug 和 Wog 广泛用于任何非常小的爬行、爬行、跳跃或飞行生物，通常被认为是一种讨厌的动物，甚至被广泛使用。对于引起疾病的完全不相关的细菌和病毒，尤其是“四处传播”的感冒：抱歉我不能去？我知道“虫子”是该组中最不具体的词，但节肢动物是包容性的。节肢动物没有脊椎；它们的特征是有关节的腿或附肢、分段的身体部位和通常坚硬的外壳。真正的昆虫属于节肢动物的特殊目，其成员有咬或吸的口器，例如臭虫。 、水蝽和植物蝽也有咬性口器，并具有覆盖和保护后翅的坚硬角质前翅。昆虫和甲虫是节肢动物中最大的一类，有近百万种。昆虫的身体分为三部分，每部分都有一对腿，总共有六条腿，这一特征将昆虫与蜘蛛区分开来，蜘蛛有八条腿，并与蝎子、螨虫和蜱虫一起生活。节肢动物的另一类是蜘蛛纲动物，包括虾、螃蟹、龙虾、藤壶和小龙虾，它们主要生活在水中或水附近，其外壳坚硬，随着体型的增大而脱落。

4.114 Build
These verbs all indicate the assembling and fitting together of materials into a structure. Build, the most general and least formal word, has the widest range of uses, from the most concrete and specific to the highly figurative and abstract. [Carpenters build houses and birds build nests; Cavemen built fires at the mouths of their caves; The company director hoped to build a business empire; Nations built their hopes for peace on the fear of nuclear war.] Construct has a much more limited range of application. It emphasizes the intricate or complex nature of a building process, where build may focus on the assembling of separate parts and the resulting connection: to build a bookcase; to construct an office building. The phrase to build a bridge emphasizes engineering problems and the workmen and equipment involved. The same distinctions hold with reference to mental activities ?build pointing to gradual, step-by-step creation through continued efforts. [Philosophers construct complicated systems for describing existence; Neurotics may be unable to build healthy relationships.] If substituted for build in the last example, construct would have an unfortunate overtone of artificiality.

这些动词都表示将材料组装和组装成结构，这是最普遍和最不正式的词，具有最广泛的用途，从最具体和具体的到高度具象和抽象的鸟类建造巢穴。在他们的洞穴口生火；公司董事希望建立一个商业帝国；各国将和平的希望建立在对核战争的恐惧之上。] 结构的应用范围更加有限。建造一个建筑过程，其中建造可能集中于各个部件的组装以及由此产生的连接：建造一个书柜；建造一座办公楼；建造一座桥梁这个短语强调了工程问题以及所涉及的工人和设备。坚持指精神活动？build 指向通过持续努力逐步进行的创造[哲学家构建复杂的系统来描述存在；神经症患者可能无法建立健康的关系。]如果在最后一个例子中替换为“build”，不幸的是，这种结构会有一种人为的暗示。

Like build, erect may involve the assembling of parts. Erect, however, chiefly stress height and vertical position, meaning to put or set something up: to erect a skyscraper; to erect a monument; They finally built a road up the Acrocorinth to the tower that had been erected centuries before. Erect also has figurative uses: to erect a tariff wall; to erect a trade barrier.

与建造一样，“竖立”也可能涉及部件的组装，但是，“竖立”主要强调高度和垂直位置，意思是放置或设置某些东西：竖立一座摩天大楼；竖立一座纪念碑；建造一条通往阿克罗科林斯的道路。几个世纪前就已经竖立起来的塔也有象征性的用途：建立关税墙；建立贸易壁垒。

Fabricate has least the sense of building a structure on its intended location. In suggesting the assembly and fitting together of parts, it implies more the standardized manufacturing of smaller items in a factory: to fabricate parts for do-it-yourself furniture-making kits. Recent techniques of house-building have, of course, perfected the prefabrication of all units, which are then shipped and assembled on the spot. Unless this type of building or construction is meant, one would still not use fabricate of house or bridge building. In other uses, the word has taken on a strong negative overtone of artificiality or falsity: a friend who fabricates flimsy stories to conceal his irresponsibility.

Fabricate 的含义至少是在预定位置建造建筑物。在暗示将零件组装和装配在一起时，它更多地意味着在工厂中标准化制造较小的物品：为 DIY 家具制作套件制造零件。当然，最近的房屋建造技术已经完善了所有单元的预制，然后运送并在现场组装。除非是指这种类型的建筑或建筑，否则人们仍然不会使用房屋或桥梁建造的 fabricate。在其他用法中，这个词具有强烈的人为或虚假的负面含义：一个编造脆弱故事来掩盖其不负责任的朋友。

	ANTONYMS: DESTROY, devastate.
	

4.115 Burn
Burn, the general word, means to effect a change in an object through the action of heat or fire. The object may be changed only slightly, or it may be totally destroyed. [A cigarette burned the finish on the table; A fire burned the house down.] Although it usually connotes some degree of destruction, burning may accomplish a useful purpose. A householder burns fuel to heat the house. In autumn, a gardener burns leaves to dispose of them. Not only heat but also extreme cold, corrosive chemicals gases, electricity, radiation, friction and the like may cause the kind of surface change or stinging sensation associated with a burn. Hence, acid is said to burn the skin and a cutting wind may make the cheek burn. Burn can also mean to cause a feeling of heat in a part of the body: The hot spices burned his mouth and tongue.

烧伤，一般指通过热或火的作用使物体发生变化。物体可能只发生轻微变化，也可能被完全毁坏。[香烟烧毁了桌子的饰面；大火烧毁了房子。] 尽管烧伤通常表示某种程度的破坏，但它也可以达到有用的目的。户主燃烧燃料来取暖。秋天，园丁焚烧树叶来处理它们。不仅热，而且极冷、腐蚀性化学气体、电、辐射、摩擦等都可能导致与烧伤相关的表面变化或刺痛感。因此，据说酸会灼伤皮肤，刺骨的寒风会使脸颊灼伤。烧伤也可以表示使身体某个部位感到热：热香料烫伤了他的嘴和舌头。

To scald is to burn with a very hot liquid or steam. Thus, the careless cook may scald herself if she spills hot soup or boiling water.

烫伤是指被非常热的液体或蒸汽烫伤。因此，如果粗心的厨师洒出热汤或开水，她可能会烫伤自己。

Singe, scorch and char are related in that they mean to burn partially, slightly or superficially. To singe is to burn the surface or ends of something: The fire singed his eyebrows. Singeing is sometimes done deliberately, as to remove bristles or to keep hair from splitting. A cook may singe a plucked chicken to remove pinfeathers by passing the fowl through an open flame. To scorch is to burn something to the point of discolouration, usually by hot metal: She scorched the dress by setting the iron too high for the fabric. Char may imply a more advanced stage of combustion. It means to reduce a substance to carbon, either completely, as in charcoal, or partially: Pieces of charred wood remained after the campfire had burnt out; the charred remains of a burnt-down house.

烧焦、灼烧和炭化彼此相关，因为它们的意思是部分、轻微或浅表燃烧。烧焦是指烧伤某物的表面或末端：火烧焦了他的眉毛。烧焦有时是故意为之，比如为了去除鬃毛或防止毛发分叉。厨师可能会将拔了毛的鸡放在明火中烤焦，以去除鸡身上的细毛。灼烧是指将某物烧到褪色的程度，通常是用热金属：她把熨斗的温度调得太高，把衣服烧焦了。炭化可能意味着燃烧的更高级阶段。它的意思是将物质完全转化为碳，比如木炭，或者部分转化为碳：篝火烧尽后剩下的烧焦的木块；被烧毁的房屋的烧焦的残骸。

Sear, brand and cauterize all connote deliberate burning to achieve a definite purpose. All are also used of flesh. Of the three, sear is the most general word, as it can mean both brand and cauterize. Searing involves the subjecting of a surface to intense heat for a very short time. This may have the effect of hardening, sealing, drying up, destroying tissue or leaving an ineradicable imprint. [Before stewing the beef, the cook seared it over high heat to seal the juices in.] To brand is to sear with a hot iron, burning a mark into the flesh, as to signify ownership. A grazier brands his cattle so that he can identify them if they stray or are stolen. To Cauterize is to sear tissue with a caustic agent or heated iron for curative purposes. A doctor may cauterize a wound to prevent infection.

Sear、brand 和 cauterize 都表示为了达到某个目的而故意烧灼。所有这些词也用于指肉体。在这三个词中，sear 是最常用的词，因为它既可以表示 brand，又可以表示 cauterize。searing 涉及将表面置于极短时间内的高温下。这可能会使其变硬、封住、变干、破坏组织或留下无法磨灭的印记。[在炖牛肉之前，厨师会用大火将其炙烤以将汁液封在里面。]brand 是用烧红的铁烙，在肉上烙出痕迹，以表明所有权。牧场主会给他的牛打上烙印，以便在它们走失或被盗时识别它们。Cauterize 是用腐蚀剂或烧红的铁烙组织以达到治疗目的。医生可能会烧灼伤口以防止感染。

SEE: COMBUSTIBLE, HOT, PASSIONATE, STIGMA.


4.116 Busy
These adjectives all refer to activity or involvement. Busy is the
least formal word. It may indicate nothing more than that a person is
working on or doing something or that a thing is in use. [Mr. Brown is
busy right now; The line is busy.] Or it may imply constant,
concentrated involvement in business or intensive and varied activity
