Compressed in this context refers to the putting of a gas under pressure to make it occupy less space: compressed air.

简洁、浓缩和压缩暗示着空间的限制逐渐增大；这种递进的用法之一是暗示写作简洁或不冗长。简洁暗示着使用的词语数量恰好足以表达某事，不多不少；它通常更适用于技术性、事实性的工作，但也可能适用于富有想象力的散文：简洁的报告；海明威的简洁句子。浓缩暗示着将较长的文章煮沸至其基本内容：浓缩的书。压缩暗示着极其简洁，但不一定是将较长的内容缩短了：用压缩的语句来解释已经浓缩的报告。浓缩和压缩在物理科学中也有特定用途。浓缩是指加热液体，使水分蒸发，剩下更致密或半固体的物质：炼乳。在这种情况下，压缩是指对气体施加压力，使其占用更少的空间：压缩空气。

Constricted suggests extreme confinement in general, with an added note of uncomfortable limitation: constricted movement in the crowded bus.

收缩通常表示极度受限，还带有一种不舒服的限制感：在拥挤的公交车上行动受限。

SEE: MINUTE, SHORTEN, SMALL, TERSE.
	ANTONYMS: extended, loose, VERBOSE.
	
	
4.167 Compare
These words refer to things that are roughly similar but not exactly alike. Compare suggests that one thing is like another in some significant way, however unlike in others: a war that compares to the Korean conflict in its evident stalemate of constructive alternatives. In the imperative, the word may also be an invitation to regard two things side by side in order to note their differences as well as their similarities: Compare these examples of Rembrandt’s early and late styles. Resemble is not readily used in the imperative, but otherwise it is closely related to compare. Its stress, however, is on a closer likeness, indicating that on thing compares in a number of ways to something else. Also, the word carries a stronger visual suggestion than compare: children who resemble their mother; a girl who resembled someone I used to know; an argument that resembles an earlier but now discredited theory.

这些词指的是大致相似但不完全相同的事物。比较表明一件事物在某些重要方面与另一件事物相似，但在其他方面却不同：一场与朝鲜战争相比的战争，其建设性选择的僵局明显。在祈使句中，这个词也可能是邀请人们将两件事物并列看待，以注意它们的不同点和相似点：比较一下伦勃朗早期和晚期风格的这些例子。类似在祈使句中不太常用，但除此之外，它与比较密切相关。但它的重点在于更紧密的相似性，表明一件事物在很多方面可以与其他事物进行比较。此外，这个词比比较带有更强烈的视觉暗示：与母亲相似的孩子；与我以前认识的某个人相似的女孩；与早期但现在已被推翻的理论相似的论点。

In many uses correspond is a more formal word for ideas suggested by resemble: an activist movement that corresponds to similar movements in the 1930s. The word has its own area of meaning, however, in suggesting things that are alike in that they match or complement each other: an availability of funds that seldom corresponds to the needs of units at work in the field. Parallel can also be used as a more formal substitute for resemble, but most often it suggests the separateness of two similar things: space research in Russia which parallels that in the United States; proposals that not only paralleled but actually preceded Darwin’s.

在很多用法中，correspond 是一个更正式的词，用来表示 Similar 所提出的想法：与 20 世纪 30 年代的类似运动相对应的激进运动。然而，该词有其自己的意义，即表示相似的东西，它们彼此匹配或互补：资金的可用性很少与现场工作单位的需求相对应。Parallel 也可以用作 Similar 的更正式替代词，但它最常用于表示两个相似事物的独立性：俄罗斯的太空研究与美国的太空研究相似；不仅与达尔文的提议相似，而且实际上早于达尔文的提议。

With approximate, the emphasis is on the roughness of the likeness: a bill that only approximated the demands of the opposition. The word may also suggest that one thing falls short of matching another in obvious fashions. Approach is like approximate in suggesting that one thing cannot measure up to something with which it is compared; the special emphasis here, however, is on quantity or volume: share-market levels that only approached previous highs. Often, the word emphasizes a lower level: a book that approaches his others in quality.

近似强调的是相似的程度：法案仅近似于反对派的要求。该词也可能暗示一件事在明显方面不如另一件事。近似与近似一样，暗示一件事无法与它所比较的​​东西相提并论；然而，这里特别强调的是数量或成交量：股票市场水平仅接近先前的高点。通常，该词强调较低的水平：一本书在质量上接近其他书。

Savour of suggests that one thing only vaguely compares to another in some almost elusive way. Thus the amount of similarity suggested is even less than for approximate and approach: a novel that savours of a feeble attempt to mimic Joyce; a northern port that nevertheless somehow savoured of the Mediterranean in its whitewashed houses and tiled roofs. While savour of can suggest equally well an advantageous or unfortunate likeness, the more pungent and colloquial smack of almost exclusively suggests an undesirable similarity: an offer that smacks of bribery. Both words tend to relate a single example to a larger category of things which it resembles, however distantly.

相似性表明一件事物与另一件事物之间只有一种几乎难以捉摸的相似性。因此，相似性所暗示的相似性甚至比近似性和方法性所暗示的还要少：一部小说带有模仿乔伊斯的微弱尝试；一座北方港口，其粉刷过的房屋和铺着瓦片的屋顶却带有地中海的味道。虽然相似性可以同样暗示有利或不利的相似性，但更刺鼻和口语化的相似性几乎只暗示一种不受欢迎的相似性：一种带有贿赂味道的提议。这两个词都倾向于将一个例子与它所相似的更大类别的事物联系起来，无论它们之间的相似性有多远。

SEE: COUNTERPART, DUPLICATE, SIMILAR.
	ANTONYMS: contrast, oppose.
	

4.168 Compel
These words all denote the urging or driving of a person to do something or the obtaining of the performance of some action, all by the use of irresistible physical or moral force. Compel may have as its agent a person, an impersonal entity, a law, an action or a set of conditions, and its object may be a person or an action. A parent may compel his child to do his lessons by threatening to suspend his allowance; the government compels young men to perform military service; the law compels one to report one’s income on pain of penalty; an attack compels one to defend oneself; a recession may compel an employer to lay off many of his employees; the government may take steps to compel compliance with the law.

这些词都表示敦促或驱使某人做某事或迫使某人执行某项行动，所有这些都是通过不可抗拒的物理或道德力量来实现的。强迫的对象可以是人、非个人的实体、法律、行动或一组条件，其客体可以是人或行动。父母可以用暂停零花钱的威胁来强迫孩子学习；政府强迫年轻人服兵役；法律强迫人们上报收入，否则将受到处罚；袭击迫使人们进行自卫；经济衰退可能迫使雇主解雇大量员工；政府可以采取措施强制人们遵守法律。

Force suggests an actual physical process, the use of power, energy or strength to accomplish something or to subdue resistance: to force a confession out of someone; to force the enemy back; to force a lock; to force someone to change an opinion; to force a smile. Coerce can imply the actual use of force but very often suggests its potential in an attempt to secure the surrender of the will: A child may be coerced into obedience by physical punishment or by the threat of it.

Force 指的是实际的物理过程，即使用权力、能量或力量来完成某件事或压制抵抗：逼迫某人认罪；逼退敌人；强行开锁；强迫某人改变观点；强迫微笑。 Coerce 可以指实际使用武力，但更常见的是暗示其潜在目的是试图确保意志的屈服：孩子可能会被体罚或体罚威胁而被迫服从。

Constrain has connotations of repression, restriction, confinement or limitation. It means to compel, but often suggests that the action being prompted or urged is in a negative direction or at least away from that which one may consider positive or pleasant: a man who was constrained by his weak heart to give up all forms of strenuous exercise.

Constrain 有压制、限制、禁锢或约束的含义。它的意思是强迫，但通常暗示所促使或敦促的行为是朝着消极的方向，或至少是远离人们可能认为积极或愉快的方向：一个人因心脏虚弱而被迫放弃所有形式的剧烈运动。

To necessitate and to oblige, as here considered, mean to make an action necessary by the imposition of conditions that must be reacted to. There is often a suggestion of urgency about these words. [Reduction of income necessitates a curtailment of spending; Courtesy obliges a man to respond to an invitation.]

此处所指的“迫使”和“应允”是指通过施加必须作出反应的条件使某项行动成为必要。这些词常常带有紧迫感。[收入减少必然导致支出减少；礼貌迫使一个人回应邀请。]

SEE: IMPEL, INDUCE, PROPEL.


4.169 Compete
These words refer to two or more people or factions struggling against each other to win a given objective. Compete is the most general of these, applying to the widest range of situations: pianists competing in the contest; football teams competing for the premiership; candidates competing for the office; armies competing for victory in the battle; businesses competing for the biggest slice of the market. As can be seen, the objective implied by this word can be, most concretely, a prize or award that is won by a single confrontation, or, more abstractly, a share in something that falls to one side for its continuing effort: television programmes competing for the largest share of the audience.

这些词语指的是两个或多个人或派系为了实现既定目标而相互竞争。竞争是这些词语中最普遍的，适用于最广泛的情况：钢琴家在比赛中竞争；足球队争夺总理职位；候选人争夺职位；军队在战斗中争夺胜利；企业争夺最大的市场份额。可以看出，这个词所暗示的目标可以最具体地是通过一次对抗赢得的奖品或奖励，或者更抽象地，可以是某物的一部分，但该物因持续努力而落败：电视节目争夺最大的观众份额。

Contend and vie suggest, more strictly, the moment of direct confrontation, and thus are narrowed to one possibility for compete. Contend, however, adds a note of actual hostility or serious disagreement, where compete may suggest none; furthermore, the word often suggests a dispute carried on verbally, as in a debate: speakers who fell to contending about the least important points in the proposal. Even when the verbal implication is not present, the animus often remains: forces contending bitterly to win the uncommitted delegates. The implications of vie stress a series of countering manoeuvres in an ongoing struggle: neighbours continually vying with each other as to who could display the greater number of status symbols. The word is, however, more like compete than contend in lacking overtones of hostility.

Contend 和 vie 更严格地表示直接对抗的时刻，因此仅限于 compete 的一种可能性。但是，Contend 增加了实际敌意或严重分歧的音调，而 compete 可能不表示任何敌意或分歧；此外，这个词通常表示口头进行的争论，如辩论：发言者开始就提案中最不重要的几点争论不休。即使没有口头暗示，敌意往往仍然存在：各方势力激烈争夺尚未表态的代表。vie 的含义强调在持续的斗争中采取一系列反击策略：邻国不断相互竞争，看谁能展示更多的地位象征。但是，这个词更像是 compete 而不是 conend，缺乏敌意的意味。

Oppose may often, by implication, restrict the competing ides to two: extroversion, as opposed to introversion; pre-selection ballots in which may compete for the right to oppose the other party’s choice in the main election. This narrowing of sides to tow is not always present in the word: a debate in which many factions opposed one another. In any case, oppose does stress the choosing of clearly defined sides and suggests a greater rigidity of position than any of these words. It may suggest hostility, like contend, or at least a serious discrepancy of views not easily compromised: attitudes towards drug addiction that were sharply opposed to each other. Rival can be specifically used to suggest a struggle of two or more sides to outdo each other: candidates who rival each other in popularity; dresses that rival each other in vulgarity. Even more specifically, the word may suggest that one performance nearly matches another: domestic wines that rival the best French imports; a role in which she rivals the best acting she has previously shown us. These special applications of the word, in this context, make it the most restricted in meaning of words grouped here.

Oppose 可能经常会暗示将竞争的思想限制为两种：外向与内向相对；预选投票中，人们可能争夺在主要选举中反对另一方选择的权利。这种将双方缩小到两方的局面并不总是出现在这个词中：一场许多派系相互对立的辩论。无论如何，oppose 确实强调选择明确界定的阵营，并且比这些词中的任何一个都更能表明立场的僵化。它可能暗示敌意，如 contend，或者至少暗示观点的严重分歧，不容易妥协：对吸毒的态度是尖锐对立的。Rival 可以专门用来表示两方或多方为超越对方而展开的斗争：候选人在受欢迎程度上相互竞争；着装在粗俗程度上相互竞争。更具体地说，这个词可能暗示一种表现几乎可以与另一种表现相媲美：国产葡萄酒可以与最好的法国进口葡萄酒相媲美；她扮演的角色可以与她之前向我们展示的最佳表演相媲美。在这个语境中，该词的这些特殊应用使其成为这里分组的词中含义最受限制的。

SEE: ARGUE, CONTROVERSY, FIGHT, OPPONENT.
		ANTONYMS: COINCIDE, collaborate, co-operate.


4.170 Competent
These words are applied to persons who exhibit more than average acquired or native skill in the performance of some act or operation. Competent attributes to the subject the ability to carry out the requirements of a specific task. By implication, the completed task is one that can be rated objectively as being either satisfactory or unsatisfactory: No competent tax accountant could possibly have made such egregious errors in making out your return. Thus, while competent can suggest expertise in a complicated field, adequacy rather than excellence may be indicated by the word. A performing artist, for example, might be insulted if described by this word: competent piano-playing that nevertheless lacked inspiration and nuance.	

这些词语适用于在执行某项行为或操作时表现出高于平均水平的后天或天生技能的人。胜任是指主体有能力完成特定任务的要求。言下之意，完成的任务可以客观地评为满意或不满意：没有一个胜任的税务会计师可能在为您报税时犯下如此严重的错误。因此，虽然胜任可以表示在复杂领域的专业知识，但这个词可能表示足够而不是优秀。例如，如果用这个词来描述一位表演艺术家，他可能会觉得受到了侮辱：熟练的钢琴演奏，但缺乏灵感和细微差别。

Able and capable at their most neutral may indicate the practicable or possible: an infant barely able to walk. Capable is stronger here in indicating potential, possibly unsuspected, whether for good or ill: a husband capable of more tenderness than his wife had ever allowed him to express; totalitarian governments capable of the most unspeakable enormities. Where the words approach competent in referring to above-average skill, able suggests versatility and resourcefulness and capable a practical, problem-solving approach: an able architect; a capable stenographer. Capable stresses trained proficiency for a specific task, whereas able suggests a wider perspective or potential: capable lawyers, well-schooled in the intricacies of company law; able children, eager for knowledge, though thwarted by a lack of training in the fundamentals of reading. Also, capable can be applied to things as well as animals: an electronic computer capable of storing millions of bits of information; a shipyard capable of producing two nuclear submarines a month. Able, on the other hand, applies only to creatures capable of performing an action.

Able 和 competent 在最中性的情况下可能表示可行或可能：刚刚不会走路的婴儿。Capable 在这里更强烈地表示潜力，可能是未被察觉的，无论是好是坏：丈夫能够比妻子允许他表达的更多温柔；极权政府能够犯下最无法形容的暴行。当这些词接近 competence 时，指的是高于平均水平的技能，able 暗示多才多艺和足智多谋，able 暗示务实的解决问题的方法：一位能干的建筑师；一位能干的速记员。Capable 强调对某项具体任务的训练熟练程度，而 able 暗示更广阔的视角或潜力：capable 律师，精通公司法的复杂性；able 孩子，渴望获得知识，但由于缺乏阅读基础的训练而受阻。此外，capable 既可以用于动物，也可以用于事物：能够存储数百万比特信息的电子计算机；每月能够生产两艘核潜艇的造船厂。另一方面，Able 仅适用于能够执行某项动作的生物。

Qualified stresses the possession of required skills and is generally applied to professions or trades for which a minimum of schooling or training is required. A qualified teacher has completed the academic training prescribed, but is not necessarily competent.

合格强调拥有所需的技能，通常适用于需要最低限度的学校教育或培训的专业或行业。合格教师已完成规定的学术培训，但不一定胜任。

Efficient adds to competent the idea of a skill in making the most of the time and material available. A mechanic who is competent and efficient will perform a repair job more quickly and cheaply than a mechanic who is merely competent.

高效是胜任的补充，指的是充分利用时间和材料的技能。胜任且高效的技工比仅仅胜任的技工更快、更便宜地完成维修工作。

Fit and good are general words often used in place of the other words in this list. Fit is usually used predicatively: the manager is not fit for his position (meaning not qualified, not competent, not efficient). The specific meaning of good, when used in this sense, is indicated by the context. A good teacher is both qualified and competent; a good manager is both competent and efficient.

Fit 和 good 是常用词，经常用来代替此列表中的其他词。Fit 通常用作表语：经理不适合担任其职位（意思是不合格、不称职、效率低下）。good 的具体含义在用作表语时由上下文决定。一位好老师既称职又称职；一位好经理既称职又高效。

SEE: ADEQUATE, EXCELLENT, GENIUS, SKILL.
	ANTONYMS: DEFICIENT, incompetent, inefficient, unfit.
	
	
4.171 Complain
These words refer to the action of finding fault with one’s circumstances. Complain is the most general and also the most neutral of these, suggesting either justified or unjustified dissatisfaction with one’s situation: They complained about the terrible brutality with which they were treated; complaining about imaginary slights from the neighbours. Bewail was once similar to complain in its neutrality, but its archaic flavour now makes it suitable only for the unsympathetic satire of complaining that is motivated by self-pity, especially when the subject is a woman: like a tedious Puccini heroine bewailing her sad fate. Grumble suggests an habitual ill-humour, especially of a man, that does not quite expect to be taken seriously: husbands who grumble every summer as they dutifully pack the car for the family holiday; prisoners grumbling over the poor quality of institutional food. Whine implies a high-pitched, self-pitying tone, often sued for a continually complaining or nagging woman or for a petulant child; its use suggests complete lack of sympathy for the subject: The patient whined on and on about how unfairly her psychoanalyst had treated her. If applied to a man, it suggests weak or cowardly behaviour: he whined about his bad luck while others put out the fire.

这些词指的是对自己的处境吹毛求疵的行为。抱怨是这些词中最普遍也是最中性的，表明对自己的处境的不满是合理或不合理的：他们抱怨自己受到的可怕残酷对待；抱怨邻居们想象中的怠慢。哀号曾经与抱怨在中立性上相似，但它的古老风格现在使它只适合用于由自怜引起的无情讽刺抱怨，尤其是当主题是女性时：就像普契尼笔下乏味的女主角哀叹她悲惨的命运。牢骚指的是习惯性的坏脾气，尤其是男人的坏脾气，并不指望被认真对待：丈夫每年夏天在为家庭度假尽职尽责地收拾行李时都会抱怨；囚犯抱怨机构食物质量差。呜咽意味着一种尖锐的、自怜的语调，通常用于不断抱怨或唠叨的女人或任性的孩子；它的用法表明对治疗对象完全缺乏同情：病人不停地抱怨她的心理分析师对她有多不公平。如果用在男人身上，则表明他软弱或胆怯：当其他人救火时，他却抱怨自己的坏运气。

The rest of these words range from the extremely informal to slang. They also range, in the order of their discussion, towards less and less sympathy for the subject. Gripe can be used for any fruitless expression of dissatisfaction, but is especially pertinent to military life: The officers were told to beware of soldiers who have nothing to gripe about. This context has emphasized the word as a normal everyday complaining about trivial things; it would not be used for outraged indignation or even serious dissatisfaction. Whinge is much more common than whine or gripe for continual petty expression of dissatisfaction: always whingeing about not getting a fair go; farmers who whinged about too much rain when they weren’t whingeing about too little. Grouse implies a greater animus than gripe or whinge and may suggest a more pointed lashing out in accusation or insult: grousing about the food only when the cook could overhear them. Beef works as an intensification of gripe but does not necessarily suggest the bitterness of grouse; it can suggest an unjustified complaining: They beefed about mistreatment only to get front-page treatment in the newspapers. Bellyache suggests complaining that is interminable, tiresome and completely without justification: continually bellyaching no matter how his room-mates tried to shut him up. The slang word bitch is extremely general in its reference to complaining; it can range in application from the fruitless dissatisfaction indicated by gripe to the bitterness of grouse: He bitched about the weather, the food and anything else that crossed his mind; The bitched about the favouritism the teacher showed to the daughter of the headmistress.

其余这些词的范围从非常不正式的到俚语。它们也随着讨论的顺序而变得越来越不同情这个话题。Gripe 可以用于任何毫无结果的不满表达，但尤其适用于军队生活：军官们被告知要提防那些没有什么可抱怨的士兵。这种语境强调了这个词是日常对琐碎事情的抱怨；它不会用于愤怒的愤慨甚至严重的不满。Whinge 比 whine 或 gripe 更常用于表达持续的琐碎不满：总是抱怨没有得到公平的待遇；农民抱怨雨水太多，而不是抱怨雨水太少。Grouse 比 gripe 或 whinge 暗示了更大的敌意，可能暗示更尖锐的指责或侮辱：只有当厨师能听到时才抱怨食物。 Beef 可以强化 gripe，但并不一定表示 grouse 的苦涩；它可以表示无理的抱怨：他们抱怨受到的虐待，结果却上了报纸头版。Bellyache 表示抱怨没完没了、令人厌烦且毫无道理：不管室友如何劝他闭嘴，他都不停地抱怨。俚语 bitch 非常笼统地指抱怨；它的应用范围很广，从 gripe 表示的毫无结果的不满到 grouse 的苦涩：他抱怨天气、食物以及他想到的任何其他事情；那个人抱怨老师偏袒女校长的女儿。

SEE: DEPLORE, DISAPPROVAL, UPSET.
	ANTONYMS: applaud, approve, PRAISE.


4.172 Comliant
These words refer to a pleasant or tolerant manner, open to other people’s demands or desires. Compliant suggests a passive nature readily moulded to conform to the wishes of others, one easily persuaded with little effort: meekly compliant to even his harshest expectations. Suggestible is a less formal word for the same idea, but it has an additional implication indicating a naïve or unguarded sensibility that can be influenced even by subtle or indirect methods: The disapproved of showing such violence-ridden films to suggestible children.

这些词指的是一种愉快或宽容的态度，对别人的要求或愿望持开放态度。Compliant 指的是一种被动的天性，很容易被塑造成顺从他人的愿望，一个人很容易被说服，几乎不用费什么力气：即使对他最苛刻的期望也温顺地顺从。Suggestible 是一个不太正式的词，表达了同样的意思，但它还有一个额外的含义，表示一种天真或不设防的敏感性，即使是通过微妙或间接的方法也能影响它：他们不赞成向易受暗示影响的儿童放映此类充斥暴力的电影。

Willing stresses a more conscious decision to do something and does not, unlike compliant or suggestible, suggest an innately weak or conforming nature: informing her that he would be willing to run the errand for her; willing, eager students. On the other hand, obliging refers not to a conscious choice but to a nature that is cheerfully ready to assist or that will permit someone else to satisfy a wish: an obliging stewardess; teenage girls who feel they must be obliging on dates or become unpopular. Agreeable stresses the cheerful side of obliging: an agreeable personality. It may also suggest anything that is simply pleasurable: an agreeable climate. But the word, in another use, can suggest an even more willing and open attitude than obliging: finding that she was agreeable to anything he suggested. Accommodating refers to people who are willing, obliging or agreeable in the sense of preparedness to do or supply what is wanted: In our search for local historical material the storekeeper was most accommodating.

愿意强调更有意识地决定做某事，与顺从或易受暗示不同，它并不表示天生软弱或顺从的天性：告诉她他愿意为她跑腿；愿意、热切的学生。另一方面，乐于助人指的不是有意识的选择，而是指乐于助人或允许他人满足愿望的天性：乐于助人的空姐；十几岁的女孩觉得在约会时必须乐于助人，否则就会不受欢迎。和蔼可亲强调乐于助人的快乐一面：和蔼可亲的个性。它也可能表示任何令人愉快的事物：宜人的气候。但是，这个词在另一种用法中，可以表示比乐于助人更愿意和更开放的态度：发现她同意他提出的任何建议。通情达理指愿意、乐于助人或和蔼可亲的人，意思是愿意做或提供所需的东西：在我们寻找当地历史资料时，店主是最乐于助人的。

Complaisant in one of its uses is simply a more formal term for agreeable or obliging, but with a greater stress on the conforming character suggested by complaint: her complaisant eagerness to please. The word has a special use, however, to suggest a cheerful or hypocritical indifference to strict moral standards, either in others or oneself: parents who are permissive and complaisant about their children’s behaviour. Broad-minded is in some ways a more informal substitute for complaisant in this context; it suggests a lax regard for moral standards, although it does not necessarily imply a cheerful attitude. In other contexts the word might suggest an admirable ability to see all sides of a question. Here, by contrast, it suggests, almost euphemistically, an ability to accept the misbehaviour of others without protest: parties that put a strain on the most broad-minded of her older friends.

Complaisant 的一种用法仅仅是表示和蔼可亲或乐于助人的更正式的术语，但更强调 complaint 所暗示的顺从性格：她那种讨人喜欢的、讨人喜欢的、讨人喜欢的热情。然而，这个词还有一种特殊的用法，表示对他人或自己的严格道德标准表现出一种愉快或虚伪的漠不关心：父母对孩子的行为宽容而顺从。Broad-minded 在某种程度上是 complaisant 的非正式替代词，在这种情况下，它表示对道德标准的宽松尊重，尽管它并不一定意味着愉快的态度。在其他情况下，这个词可能表示一种令人钦佩的全面看待问题的能力。相比之下，在这里，它几乎委婉地表示一种不抗议地接受他人不当行为的能力：给她最宽容的老朋友带来压力的聚会。

SEE: ADAPTABLE, LENIENT, MALLEABLE.
	ANTONYMS: narrow-minded, STUBBORN, UNWILLING, WILFUL.

4.173 Component
These words all refer to parts of a whole. Component refers to a part that functions in association with other parts but that can easily be detached from them; this is in contrast to an organic whole in which the parts are fused or have lost their individual identity within the larger entity. In choosing hi-fi equipment, for example, one can buy separate component, such as speakers, turntable and amplifier, and wire them together oneself. Or one can buy a pre-packaged console, designed as a single unit. The word can suggest a more intimate relationship, as in chemistry, where it refers to a substance that in varying degrees is present in a mixture without being chemically integrated into it; in this case, a change in appearance or apparent loss of identity may be indicated: Salt is a component of sea water. Ingredient is a more general word, referring equally well to the unaltered substances mixed together in an amorphous mass and to the fused or transformed parts of an entity or organic whole: Turmeric is an ingredient of curry powder; a novel that contains all the ingredients of good mystery story.

这些词都指整体的各部分。组件指与其他部分协同工作但又很容易从其他部分分离的部分；这与有机整体形成对比，在有机整体中，各部分融合在一起或失去其在较大实体中的个体身份。例如，在选择高保真设备时，人们可以购买单独的组件，如扬声器、转盘和放大器，然后自己将它们连接在一起。或者，人们可以购买预先包装好的控制台，设计为一个单元。这个词可以表示更密切的关系，例如在化学中，它指的是以不同程度存在于混合物中但未化学整合的物质；在这种情况下，可能表示外观发生变化或身份明显丧失：盐是海水的成分。成分是一个更通用的词，同样指混合在一起形成无定形团块的未改变物质以及实体或有机整体的融合或转化部分：姜黄是咖喱粉的成分；一部小说包含了优秀悬疑故事的所有成分。

Element and constituent both refer more strictly to essential, necessary or intrinsic parts of a whole. Element comes from a Latin root meaning first principal; this is reflected in its use to indicate the rudiments of a subject: the elements of good writing. As in this example, the word’s stress is often on simple or basic parts of a more complex whole. In chemistry, the word refers to those basic substances, such as oxygen, mercury and copper, that are irreducible by ordinary chemical mans and that are the building blocks of all matter. Constituent refers more generally to a part that is necessary to the functioning of a whole. Such a part often loses it individual identity completely in contributing to the new entity; conversely, withdrawing it from the whole would drastically change the larger entity: The element hydrogen is a constituent of water.

元素和成分都更严格地指整体的基本、必要或固有部分。元素来自拉丁语词根，意为第一要素；这反映在其用来表示一门学科的基本知识：优秀写作的要素。如在本例中，这个词的重音通常放在更复杂整体的简单或基本部分上。在化学中，这个词指的是那些基本物质，例如氧、汞和铜，它们是普通化学家用来还原的，是所有物质的组成部分。成分更一般地指整体运作所必需的部分。这样的部分往往会在对新实体做出贡献时完全失去其个体身份；相反，将其从整体中撤出将彻底改变更大的实体：氢元素是水的成分。

SEE: ADDITION, PART.
	ANTONYMS: entity, WHOLE.

	
4.174 Composition
These words refer to pieces of non-fiction writing. Composition、 indicates a formal work that is planned in advance rather than improvisatory in character. It is used to refer any sort of writing assignment in school, often on a set subject, with an emphasis on grammar and style rather than on research or factual presentation: The teacher asked them to describe their summer holidays in the class composition. Exercise is a less formal word and is restricted in reference to such an assigned piece of writing in school. The word emphasizes organization round a single topic, may suggest briefer treatment, and is even less likely than composition to require factual research: a class exercise of three hundred words. Theme is sometimes used in a similar sense, but this word’s main function is to refer to the dominant idea of any piece of writing: the theme of alienation in his study of middle-class culture.
	
这些词指的是非虚构作品。Composition、 表示事先计划好的正式作品，而非即兴创作。它用于指学校里的任何写作作业，通常针对固定主题，注重语法和风格而不是研究或事实陈述：老师要求他们在课堂作文中描述他们的暑假。Exercise 是一个不太正式的词，仅指学校指定的这种写作作品。这个词强调围绕单一主题的组织，可能建议更简短的处理，甚至比 Composition 更不需要事实研究：一项三百字的课堂练习。Theme 有时以类似的意义使用，但这个词的主要功能是指任何作品的主导思想：他对中产阶级文化研究中的异化主题。

Essay is a much more general word than those above. While it may be used in place of any of them to refer to a writing assignment in school, the word more widely indicates any sort of non-fiction writing shorter than book-length, whether scholarly, humorous, propagandist or reflective. The word, moreover, may suggest any approach from the extremely informal and personal to the solemn, stately or stylized: the refreshing irreverence of Addis’s chatty essays; the Ciceronian elegance that Carlyle attempted in his early essays; howlingly funny about the perils of suburban living. Article is restricted to any piece of non-fiction that has appeared in a newspaper, magazine or journal; it ranges in reference from the briefest and most utilitarian news release through all the possibilities inherent in essay, including the more abstruse scholarly or scientific study: an article giving up-to-the-minute election returns; an article treating the effects of radiation on arthropods.

散文比上述单词更通用。虽然它可以代替上述单词中的任何一个来指代学校的写作作业，但这个词更广泛地表示任何短于书本长度的非小说写作，无论是学术性的、幽默性的、宣传性的还是反思性的。此外，这个词可能表示从极其非正式和个人化到庄严、庄重或风格化的任何方法：阿迪斯闲聊散文中令人耳目一新的不敬；卡莱尔在早期散文中试图表现出的西塞罗式的优雅；关于郊区生活危险的极其有趣的描述。文章仅限于任何出现在报纸、杂志或期刊上的非小说作品；它的范围从最简短和最实用的新闻稿到散文中固有的所有可能性，包括更深奥的学术或科学研究：一篇提供最新选举结果的文章；一篇讨论辐射对节肢动物影响的文章。

Paper has two areas of relevance. One relates to composition or exercise in referring to a written assignment for a school class or to a tutorial exercise for a university group. [His paper was well received by the class.] In this use, the word may suggest any sort of approach, from a demonstration of writing ability to the presentation of factual research. The word’s other use refers to a scholarly essay read to one’s colleagues or to a scholarly article published in a learned journal: a paper on disturbances in the earth’s magnetic field. Treatise indicates an exclusively scholarly context, referring to any presentation from essay- to book-length in which conclusions are drawn from a body of data in a formal and systematic way: a treatise on the development of the Gregorian chant.

论文有两个相关领域。一个与写作或练习有关，指的是学校课堂的书面作业或大学小组的辅导练习。[他的论文受到了全班同学的好评。] 在这种用法中，这个词可能表示任何类型的方法，从写作能力的展示到事实研究的展示。这个词的另一个用法是指向同事朗读的学术论文或发表在学术期刊上的学术文章：一篇关于地球磁场扰动的论文。论文表示一种纯粹的学术背景，指的是从论文到书籍长度的任何展示，其中以正式和系统的方式从一组数据中得出结论：一篇关于格里高利圣咏发展的论文。

The remaining pair of words also is restricted to a scholarly or academic context. Thesis may suggest briefer or less exhaustive treatment that treatise, pointing to the establishing and defending of a principle: a thesis in which he corroborates Keynes’s theory of deficit spending. Like theme, thesis may also refer to the dominant idea of contention of a piece of writing, although it pertains mainly to argumentative non-fiction: a collection of essays each of which illustrates his thesis that modern novelists are unable to create memorable women characters. Most concretely, thesis refers to the extended paper, possibly of book-length, that is sometimes required of candidates for a Master’s degree and always for a Ph.D. degree. Dissertation is the most formal of these words and, when used instead of thesis, suggests the most formal sort of writing as well. It may refer to any reasoned treatment, like treatise, but most concretely it indicates such a work, usually of book-length, when it is a requirement for a Ph.D. or other doctoral degree: a dissertation analyzing cold-war strategies. The word may sometimes be used pejoratively for any long-winded and pompous piece of exposition; giving us another dreary dissertation on the evils of imperialism.

剩下的两个词也仅限于学术或学术背景。论文可能比论文更简短或更不详尽的处理，指向建立和捍卫一个原则：他在论文中证实了凯恩斯的赤字支出理论。与主题一样，论文也可能指一篇文章的主导论点，尽管它主要涉及议论文：一系列散文，每一篇都说明了他的论点，即现代小说家无法创造令人难忘的女性角色。最具体地说，论文是指扩展的论文，可能是一本书的长度，有时是硕士学位候选人的要求，而博士学位候选人则总是要求。论文是这些词中最正式的，当用来代替论文时，也表明最正式的写作类型。它可以指任何有理有据的处理，如论文，但最具体地说，它表示这样的作品，通常是一本书的长度，当它是博士学位的要求时。或其他博士学位：分析冷战战略的论文。这个词有时可能被贬义为任何冗长而浮夸的论述；给我们另一篇关于帝国主义罪恶的沉闷论文。

SEE: REPORT, WRITE.


4.175 Compulsory
These words describe actions that are judged to be inescapably necessary. Compulsory suggests that someone in authority has imposed a course of action that may not be departed from compulsory attendance of classes. It may further suggest that the compulsory ruling will be enforcing, by coercion if necessary, and that violators will be punished: compulsory blacklisting. Mandatory is like compulsory in suggesting an imposed rule: mandatory silence in the library. In contrast, it is milder than compulsory in that it stops short of suggesting coercion and punishment as methods of enforcing the ruling.

这些词语描述了被判定为不可避免地必要的行为。强制性表明权威人士强加了一系列行动，这些行动不能偏离强制上课的规定。它还可能表明强制裁决将强制执行，必要时将使用胁迫手段，违反者将受到惩罚：强制列入黑名单。强制性与强制性一样，都表明了强加的规则：图书馆内强制保持安静。相比之下，强制性比强制性更温和，因为它没有暗示强制和惩罚是执行裁决的方法。

Binding also describes a ruling handed down by an authority, but it may specifically suggest a one-time decision concerning a specific dispute between two parties who agree beforehand to abide by the results: binding arbitration. It may also suggest that earlier, more tentative rulings have been submitted to a final authority. [The teacher’s compulsory ruling against wearing Bermuda shorts to class was referred to the principal, whose decision would be binding.]

约束性也指由权威机构做出的裁决，但它可能特别指针对双方事先同意遵守结果的特定争议做出的一次性决定：约束性仲裁。它也可能指早些时候，更临时的裁决已提交给最终权威机构。[老师禁止穿百慕大短裤上课的强制性裁决已提交给校长，校长的决定具有约束力。]

Obligatory is like binding in its legal sense. In a more general use, however, it suggests something expected or made necessary by morality or conscience, rather than by a higher authority as in the previous words: the obligatory chaperone at teenage parties. As such, its force is more what should be done than what is or must be done: attendance at tutorial classes is obligatory. Imperative refers to a necessity dictated by circumstance rather than by an authority or a code of morality: imperative to get food and water before sundown. If used to refer to an imposed rule, it is more like mandatory than compulsory.

义务在法律意义上类似于约束。然而，在更普遍的用法中，它表示道德或良知所期望或必须做的事情，而不是像前面的单词那样由更高的权威所要求或必须做的事情：青少年聚会上的义务监护人。因此，其效力更多的是应该做的事情，而不是必须做的事情：参加辅导班是义务。命令是指由环境而不是权威或道德准则决定的必要性：日落前必须获得食物和水。如果用来指强加的规则，它更像是强制性的而不是强制性的。

De rigueur is close to obligatory, but is milder in referring to those acts or observance considered necessary according to etiquette or required by good form; it usually appears only as a predicate adjective: an unwritten rule that made evening dress de rigueur for attending her soirées.

De rigueur 接近于义务，但在指代礼仪所认为必要或良好形式所要求的行为或遵守时，其语气较为温和；它通常只作为谓语形容词出现：一条不成文的规定，规定晚礼服是参加晚会的必需品。

SEE: INEVITABLE, REQUIRE, SURE.
	ANTONYMS: LENIENT, optional, unnecessary.
	
	
4.176 Conceited
These words refer to a person who is afflicted with unwarranted self-admiration or a feeling of his own superiority. Conceited pertains to an excessive affection for oneself that may be revealed by an uncritical smugness and aloofness from others: conceited girls who walk home from school with their noses in the air. More specifically, the word may point to a person who becomes well-headed because of a particular accomplishment or occurrence, often a trivial one: She became unbearably conceited after the football captain asked her out. Vain suggests a person who is extremely concerned about his personal appearance or the impression he makes on others. A conceited person might feel that his superiority is self-evident, whereas a vain person would more likely strive constantly to impress others or improve his appearance: The typical dandy of old was so vain about his appearance that he spent almost as much time primping before a mirror as his female counterpart.

这些词指的是被不合理的自我崇拜或自以为是所困扰的人。自负是指对自己的过度喜爱，这种喜爱可能表现为不加批判的自鸣得意和对他人漠不关心：自负的女孩们昂首阔步地从学校走回家。更具体地说，这个词可能指的是因为某项成就或事件（通常是微不足道的成就或事件）而变得自以为是的人：在足球队长约她出去之后，她变得自负得令人难以忍受。虚荣指的是极度关心自己外表或给别人留下的印象的人。自负的人可能觉得自己的优越性是不言而喻的，而虚荣的人则更有可能不断努力给别人留下深刻印象或改善自己的外表：典型的老花花公子对自己的外表非常自负，以至于他花在镜子前打扮的时间几乎和他的女伴一样多。

Egotistical need not suggest an outward show, like vain, so much as an extreme self-preoccupation and lack of interest in the feelings or affairs of others. On the other hand, where conceited usually suggests that someone is self-admiring for clearly defined reasons, however specious, egotistical may suggest a more unconscious, narcissistic habit of mind: an egotistical snob who thought the world began and ended where he lived. Sometimes, however, the word can point to the habit of calling attention to oneself and one’s accomplishments, while ignoring the interests of others: the egotistical artist who monopolized the conversation with talk of his work in progress.

自负不一定意味着一种外在的表现，如虚荣，而是一种极端的自我中心主义，对他人感受或事务缺乏兴趣。另一方面，自负通常意味着某人出于明确的理由而自恋，无论理由多么似是而非，而自负可能意味着一种更无意识的自恋习惯：一个自负的势利小人，认为世界从他居住的地方开始和结束。然而，有时，这个词可以指一种习惯，即把注意力集中在自己和自己的成就上，而忽视他人的利益：一个自负的艺术家，用他正在进行的工作的谈论垄断了谈话。

Boastful and vainglorious concentrate on this last possibility of egotistical, both referring to self-praise and attention-seeking in public. Boastful emphasizes unsubtle and even boorish public displays of vocal self-approval: after a few drinks, he always became boastful about his wartime activities. Vainglorious focuses more exclusively on hollow show, boastful self-praise, but conspicuous displays of status symbols are often involves: vainglorious dowagers dripping minks and diamonds.

Boastful 和 vainglorious 集中于自负的最后可能性，两者都指在公共场合自我吹嘘和寻求关注。Boastful 强调公开地、毫不掩饰地甚至粗鲁地展示自己的口头自我认可：喝了几杯酒后，他总是吹嘘自己的战时活动。Vainglorious 更专注于空洞的炫耀、自吹自擂，但经常涉及炫耀地位象征：虚荣的贵妇身上挂满了貂皮和钻石。

Proud can, of cause, indicate legitimate satisfaction at accomplishing a goal or honour: proud of his high marks in the examination. It can also apply to things invested with real dignity: a proud history; proud mountains silhouetted in the sunset. When the word takes on a disapproving tone, it suggests a stiff-necked and unrealistic lack of humility: too proud to admit that he had been grossly in error.

当然，骄傲可以表示实现目标或荣誉后感到的正当满足：为自己在考试中取得的高分感到自豪。它也可以用于形容具有真正尊严的事物：令人骄傲的历史；夕阳下映衬的令人骄傲的山脉。当这个词带有不赞同的语气时，它表明一个人固执己见，不切实际，缺乏谦逊：太骄傲了，不愿承认自己犯了严重错误。

SEE: BOAST, CONFIDENCE, EGOISM, OVERBEARING.
	ANTONYMS: deferent, humble, MODEST, TIMID.
	

4.177 Conclusive
These words are concerned with those moments in a sequence of events that are crucial to bringing about a given result. Conclusive suggests a final act that settles questions at issue in a previous course of action: the atomic-bombing of Hiroshima as the conclusive event of World War II. The word may be used in another sense to refer, not to the events themselves, but to a later analysis of them. In this sense, conclusive refers to an incontrovertible interpretation of these events as a whole: conclusive proof that Richard II was not the villain Shakespeare made him out to be. A decisive event differs from a conclusive event in that it need not necessarily be the last one in a given sequence. Indeed, it may be a situation present almost at the outset, with the whole following course of action merely corroborating it. [The enemy’s lack of inspired leadership was decisive to its defeat, long before a single shot was fired.]

这些词语与一系列事件中对实现特定结果至关重要的时刻有关。决定性事件是指解决先前行动过程中存在争议的问题的最后一项行动：广岛原子弹爆炸是第二次世界大战的决定性事件。这个词也可以用在另一种意义上，指的不是事件本身，而是对它们的后续分析。在这个意义上，决定性事件是指对这些事件整体的无可辩驳的解释：确凿的证据证明理查二世不是莎士比亚笔下的恶棍。决定性事件与决定性事件的不同之处在于，它不一定是给定序列中的最后一个事件。事实上，它可能是一种几乎在一开始就存在的情况，而整个后续行动只是证实了这一点。[敌人缺乏鼓舞人心的领导是其失败的决定性因素，早在开枪之前。]

Determining, like decisive, may refer to something that comes early or late in a course of action. Decisive may be more suitable in describe underlying factors that are inherent in a situation and prejudice the outcome. [No matter how many decisive victories Justinian won, the split of East and West into two alien cultures was the determining factor in his ultimate failure to re-unite the Roman Empire.]

决定性，就像决定性一样，可能指在行动过程中出现得早或晚的事情。决定性可能更适合描述情况中固有的、影响结果的潜在因素。[无论查士丁尼赢得了多少决定性的胜利，东西方分裂为两种异质文化是他最终未能重新统一罗马帝国的决定性因素。]

Definitive, when referring to an act, combines the meanings of both conclusive and decisive. It applies when a sequence of events has been in doubt until the very last act, which irrevocably settles things: Elizabeth’s definitive victory over the Armada settled the question of British naval superiority for centuries. When the word refers to a later analysis of event, it takes in all that is implied by conclusive in this sense, but adds to it implications of authoritative accuracy and incontestable interpretation not to be surpassed. In this sense, definitive, unlike conclusive, need not suggest the settling of controversy or the proposing of any thesis whatsoever; it simply suggests finality of examination and analysis: the definitive history of the Boer War; the definitive biography of Byron that strips away all myth and conjecture to show us the actual man as he was.

权威性在指代某一行为时，兼具了决定性和决定性的含义。它适用于一系列事件直到最后一幕才确定下来的情况：伊丽莎白对无敌舰队的决定性胜利解决了几个世纪以来英国海军优势的问题。当这个词指代对事件的后续分析时，它包含了权威性所暗示的一切，但还增加了权威准确性和无可争辩的解释的含义，这些含义是不可超越的。在这个意义上，权威性与权威性不同，它不一定意味着争议的解决或任何论点的提出；它只是表明了审查和分析的终结：布尔战争的权威历史；拜伦的权威传记，它剥去了所有的神话和猜测，向我们展示了他真实的一面。

SEE: FINAL, OUTSTANDING, SIGNIFICANT.
	ANTONYMS: inconclusive, indeterminate, PROVISIONAL, tentative.

	
4.178 Condescend
These words refer to the treating of another person as one’s inferior. Condescend suggests particularly the awareness of a social or class distinction, false or real, which one person bridges in dealing or speaking to someone beneath him. The person who condescends, however, calls attention to the difference and does not wish it forgotten. Once, this word was simply descriptive: Her Highness condescends to recognize the foreign ambassador. Nowadays, in our egalitarian world, the word has an almost exclusively negative implication: tourists who condescend to the "natives." Deign emphasizes choice; it implies that one could very well have chosen an opposite, perhaps more appropriate, course. It is not necessarily restricted solely to dealing with one’s inferiors: He didn’t deign to reply to his colleague’s accusation. The word’s extreme formality limits its use today, except for satirical effect: the salesgirl who actually deigned to wait on me.

这些词指的是将他人视为自己的下级。屈尊特别表明一个人意识到了社会或阶级差异，无论是虚假的还是真实的，一个人在与比他低的人打交道或交谈时会弥合这种差异。然而，屈尊的人会让人们注意到这种差异，并且不希望它被遗忘。曾经，这个词只是描述性的：女王陛下屈尊承认外国大使。如今，在我们这个平等的世界里，这个词几乎完全具有负面含义：屈尊对待“当地人”的游客。屈尊强调选择；它意味着一个人完全可以选择相反的、也许更合适的做法。它不一定仅限于与下级打交道：他没有屈尊回应同事的指控。这个词的极端正式性限制了它在今天的使用，除了讽刺效果：实际上屈尊为我服务的女售货员。

Stoop was earlier like condescend in emphasizing social station and like deign in suggesting choice; but it now has uses mostly relating to a discreditable moral act: statesmen who stoop to exchanging political favours. Condescend might suggest a generally grand, arch or pompous behavior; stoop suggests single questionable acts. Unbend is more like condescend on this score, but its overtone is one of approval for a stuffy person who learns to relax or act less officiously. [Why does she have to condescend to me all the time? Can’t she unbend a little and treat me like anyone else?]

以前，stoop 和 condescend 一样强调社会地位，和 deign 一样暗示选择；但现在它的用法主要与不光彩的道德行为有关：屈尊交换政治恩惠的政治家。condescend 可能暗示一种普遍的、傲慢的或自负的行为；stoop 则暗示单一的可疑行为。Unbend 在这一点上更像 condescend，但它的弦外之音是赞同一个学会放松或不那么爱管闲事的古板的人。[她为什么总是要屈尊俯就我？她就不能放开一点，把我当成别人一样对待吗？]

Patronize, even more than condescend, suggests haughtiness of bearing and an overtone of looking down on someone: a teacher who patronized his students by oversimplifying everything he taught them. Tolerate, in this context, has gone through several changes in usage. It has meant and can still mean simply to accept; society women who will tolerate eccentric guests so long as they are artists. The word at one point took on a note of reconciliation: learning to tolerate minority groups. Now this last use is avoided as resembling patronize or condescend too closely: Aboriginess who wish to be accepted, not merely tolerated.

Patronize 比 condescend 更能暗示出傲慢的态度和轻视他人的意味：一位老师通过过度简化他所教的一切来居高临下地对待学生。在这种情况下，Tolerate 的用法经历了几次变化。它曾经意味着并且仍然可以意味着接受；社交女性会容忍古怪的客人，只要他们是艺术家。这个词一度带有和解的意味：学会容忍少数群体。现在人们避免使用最后一种用法，因为它与 patronize 或 condescend 太过相似：希望被接受而不仅仅是被容忍的原住民。

SEE: OVERBEARING.
	ANTONYMS: accept, respect, REVERE.
	
	
4.179 Confidence
These words refer to a psychological trait that involves a conviction of one’s own worth or an unselfconscious certainty of succeeding at whatever is attempted, unhampered by doubt, hesitation or fear. Confidence stresses a general optimism that all is or will be well: able to face the future with confidence. The word may suggest fearless trust, whether well- or ill-advised: talking to the unsavoury people in the bar with effortless confidence. Self-confidence restricts these possibilities to a general optimism concerning one’s own capacities and accomplishment, suggesting a complete absence of timidity and, less positively, an aggressive bearing: social clubs set up to promote self-confidence in teenagers; a garish costume that matched the self-confidence with which she ploughed her way through the startled guests.

这些词语指的是一种心理特征，包括对自身价值的坚信或对成功无意识的确定，无论尝试什么，都不会受到怀疑、犹豫或恐惧的阻碍。自信强调一种普遍的乐观态度，认为一切都会好起来：能够满怀信心地面对未来。这个词可能表示无所畏惧的信任，无论是明智的还是错误的：在酒吧里毫不费力地自信地与令人讨厌的人交谈。自信将这些可能性限制为对自身能力和成就的普遍乐观，表明完全没有胆怯，以及不那么积极的攻击性举止：为促进青少年自信而设立的社交俱乐部；她在吃惊的客人中艰难前行时所穿的花哨服装与自信相匹配。

Aplomb and self-possession stress the ability to keep oneself under firm control. Self-possession suggests the restraining of conflicting impulses or the brushing aside of distractions, accompanied by a cool unemotional approach even in trying situations: calmly working her way through the customs inspection with unflustered self-possession. Aplomb, by contrast, emphasizes a total lack of self-doubt and may suggest a carefree or uncritical exuberance: Although he had never duelled before, he faced his opponent with aplomb.

泰然自若和镇定自若强调的是能够牢牢控制自己。镇定自若意味着克制冲突的冲动或排除干扰，即使在困难的情况下也能保持冷静、不带感情的态度：镇定自若地通过海关检查。相比之下，泰然自若强调的是完全没有自我怀疑，可能暗示着一种无忧无虑或不加批判的热情：尽管他以前从未决斗过，但他还是泰然自若地面对对手。

Poise stresses steadiness and balance and, somewhat like self-possession, suggests a calm sureness of manner able to cope courteously with any contingency: a shy and awkward adolescent who had turned overnight into a young woman amply endowed with grace and poise. With its emphasis on a mastery of social properties, savoir faire relates closely to poise in stressing an intuitive ability to do the right thing socially and to get on well with other people whatever the situation: a savoir faire that never deserted him whether he found himself among first-nighters at the opera or among the bare-footed habitués of a bohemian coffee shop.

风度强调稳定和平衡，有点像镇定，暗示着一种冷静、自信的态度，能够礼貌地应对任何突发事件：一个害羞、笨拙的青少年一夜之间变成了一个拥有充分的优雅和风度的年轻女子。 处事技巧强调对社交属性的掌握，与风度密切相关，强调一种直觉能力，无论在什么情况下，都能在社交中做正确的事，与他人相处融洽：无论是在歌剧院的首映式观众中，还是在波西米亚咖啡馆赤脚的常客中，他都不会抛弃这种处事技巧。

Self-assurance and smugness stress an extreme conviction of one’s own worth, ability or superiority. Self-assurance can be used either positively or negatively, but smugness is exclusively disapproving: an astonishing self-assurance in whizzing through an exam for which he had spent only a few hours preparing; insisting with unblushing self-assurance that even the stupidest native would understand her English if only she spoke loudly and clearly enough. Smugness suggests an uncritical vanity or pride in one’s own privileged position and a failure to see things from other people’s point of view. This puts it in strong contrast to savoir faire which stresses a sensing of what people will find pleasant and apt: the smugness with which she chose to stay at the most expensive hotels to avoid rubbing shoulders with the "hoi polloi." Cockiness is an informal term for complete confidence in oneself. Unlike self-assurance, the word carries some pejorative connotations and the attitude that it describes is much more in evidence than smugness: His cockiness about his athletic prowess knew no bounds.

自信和自鸣得意强调对自己的价值、能力或优越性的极度自信。自信既可以用作正面词，也可以用作负面词，但自鸣得意完全是反对的意思：她只花了几个小时准备考试，却表现出惊人的自信；她毫不掩饰地坚持认为，只要她说话声音大、语气清晰，即使是最愚蠢的当地人也能听懂她的英语。自鸣得意意味着对自己的特权地位不加批判的虚荣心或骄傲，以及无法从别人的角度看问题。这与处事处事形成鲜明对比，处事处事强调对人们会觉得愉快和合适的事物的感觉：她自鸣得意地选择住在最昂贵的酒店，以避免与“平民百姓”打交道。自大是一个非正式的术语，表示对自己完全有信心。与自信不同，这个词带有一些贬义，它所描述的态度比自鸣得意更为明显：他对自己运动能力的自信毫无止境。

SEE: EGOISM, JAUNTY, OVERBEARING, ZEST.
	ANTONYMS: ANXIETY, diffidence, DOUBT, hesitation, shyness, timidity.

	
4.180 Confine
These words refer to the shutting up, usually of people, in a particular place. Confine is the most general of these and indicates a reduction of mobility for whatever reason: He felt confined and claustrophobic in a big city; confined by ill-health to her bed. More pertinent to this context, the word suggests removing someone to a prison or mental hospital, usually against the person’s will: a sentence confining him to life imprisonment; a court order confining him indefinitely to an institution for the criminally insane. From one sense of being kept in bed, confine is used (usually in the passive voice) to mean being brought to bed pending the birth of a child: She was confined in the local hospital, awaiting her fifth baby.

这些词指将人关在某个特定的地方。Confine 是这些词中最常用的，表示由于某种原因活动能力的降低：他在大城市里感到局促不安，有幽闭恐惧症；因健康不佳而卧床不起。更切合此语境的是，这个词指将某人送进监狱或精神病院，通常是违背其意愿的：判处其终身监禁的判决；将他无限期关进精神病罪犯收容所的法院命令。从被关在床上的意思来看，confine 被用来（通常用被动语态）表示在孩子出生前被带到床上：她被关在当地医院，等待着她的第五个孩子。

The directness and informality of gaol makes confine sound euphemistic by comparison when it refers to shutting someone up in prison: gaoled on a disorderly-conduct charge. Although identical in meaning to gaol, imprison gives more formal tone without sounding= euphemistic like confine: a régime that imprisoned anyone suspected of dissent. The one possible difference between gaol and imprison is that gaol might be used for a relatively short stay: gaoled overnight because he had trouble raising bail; imprisoned for ten years in the Bastille. Incarcerate is the most formal of all these words; while close in meaning to imprison, it may suggest the initial act of imprisoning: He was incarcerated in the local gaol pending transfer to a maximum-security prison. Incarcerated is sometimes used to suggest a harsh, punitive or brutal imprisoning under inhumane conditions: They incarcerated him in a windowless basement cell. The word, furthermore, can refer like confine to the shutting up of the mentally ill; here the emphasis may be on inhumane treatment: The family incarcerated the wretch in a concealed, airless room in the attic.

相比之下，当 gaol 指的是将某人关进监狱时，其直接性和非正式性使 confine 听起来更加委婉：因扰乱治安罪名被关进监狱。尽管 imprison 的意思与 gaol 相同，但它语气更正式，而听起来又不像 confine 那样委婉：监禁任何涉嫌持不同政见者的政权。gaol 和 imprison 之间一个可能的区别是 gaol 可能用于相对较短的监禁：因为难以筹集保释金而被关进监狱过夜；在巴士底狱被监禁了十年。Incarcerate 是所有这些词中最正式的；虽然意思与 imprison 相近，但它可能暗示最初的监禁行为：他被关在当地监狱等待转移到最高安全监狱。Incarcerated 有时用于暗示在非人道条件下进行的严厉、惩罚性或野蛮的监禁：他们把他关押在一个没有窗户的地下室牢房里。此外，这个词还可以像“confine”一样指将精神病患者关起来；在这里可能强调的是非人道的待遇：这家人把这个可怜的人关在阁楼一个隐蔽的、不通风的房间里。

Intern is unique among this group, in pertaining to the impounding of people or even equipment, as during war: the policy of interning citizens of German origin during World War II. The word, furthermore, contrasts sharply with the punitive possibilities of gaol, imprison and incarcerate, in that the interning can conceivably be done for the internee’s own good: They interned the demonstrators to protect them from the fury of the mob.

拘留是这一群体中独一无二的词，它与扣押人员甚至设备有关，例如在战争期间：二战期间拘留德裔公民的政策。此外，这个词与监禁、监禁和监禁等惩罚性措施形成了鲜明对比，因为拘留可能是为了被拘留者自己的利益：他们拘留示威者是为了保护他们免受暴徒的暴怒。

SEE: CIRCUMSCRIBE.
	ANTONYMS: emancipate, free, liberate, release.


4.181 Confuse


	
	
************************************************************************************
************************************************************************************
4.613 Novel
These words refer to extended works of imaginative prose. Novel is the most specific and exact of these words, referring to any lengthy prose narrative that normally has a plot, characters, action and dialogue, but that does not refer to real people or events: best-selling novels; those who consider Don Quixote the first full-length novel. By contrast, fiction is more general since it is the group word for all forms of imaginative prose, including the short story, the novella and the novel. Since the novel is in one sense the most important form of fiction, the group word is often used with a special pertinence to this one form: a poor year for fiction in that no new major novel emerged.

这些词指的是长篇想象性散文作品。小说novel是这些词中最具体、最准确的，指的是任何长篇叙事散文，通常有情节、人物、动作和对话，但不指真实人物或事件：畅销小说；那些认为《堂吉诃德》是第一部长篇小说的人。相比之下，fiction更通用，因为它是所有形式的想象性散文的集合词，包括短篇小说、中篇小说和长篇小说。由于novel在某种意义上是最重要的小说形式，因此这个集合词通常与这种形式特别相关：这是小说的萧条年份，没有出现新的主流小说。

Romance is more difficult to pin down to an exact meaning. A related word in German is equivalent to our word novel, reflecting the development of the novel out of accounts of fabulous or legendary materials in the Middle Ages. In literary discussions, romance is often restricted to works showing works showing this emphasis on the fabulous or legendary, or it may be used more broadly to apply to novels with a strong mythic or allegorical bent: Malory’s gathering together and rewriting of the Arthurian romances; Hawthorne’s novels seen as being essentially romances. Contrary to a popular misconception, the word would never in any literary use refer merely to fiction that concerns itself with love affairs.

romance的确切含义更难确定。德语中有一个相关词，相当于我们的“novel”一词，反映了中世纪小说从神话或传奇材料中发展而来的过程。在文学讨论中，浪漫通常仅限于强调神话或传奇的作品，或者可以更广泛地用于具有强烈神话或寓言倾向的小说：马洛里的收集和重写了亚瑟王的浪漫故事；霍桑的小说被视为本质上是浪漫故事。与普遍的误解相反，这个词在任何文学用法中都不会仅指涉及爱情故事的小说。

While story most commonly is an abbreviated way of referring to an established form, the short story, it is sometimes used loosely and informally for any work of fiction with narrative thrust: novelists who concentrate on telling stories filled with physical violence. The word is also sometimes applied to the plot element of any fiction: a brief paragraph summarizing the story of the novel.

虽然“story”一词最常见的用法是指短篇小说这一既定形式，但有时也被随意地、非正式地用于指任何具有叙事主旨的小说作品：专注于讲述充满暴力故事的小说家。这个词有时也适用于任何小说的情节元素：一个简短的段落，概括小说的故事。

SEE: COMPOSITION, NARRATIVE, POETRY.
	ANTONYMS: non-fiction.
